iuseppe ario ammarco 13 ecember 1868, although some sources say 1867 – 24 anuary 1930 was an talian operatic baritone noted for his acting ability.

iography
ammarco was born in alermo, icily, and studied locally with ntonio antelli. e made his operatic début in alermo as alentine in aust operaaust in 1888. e subsequently sang to acclaim in ilan at a cala, talys most celebrated theatre, uenos ires and ondon. etween 1904 and 1919 he appeared intermittently, in 26 different roles, at the oyal pera ouse, ovent arden.

n ew ork ity, he was hired by scar ammerstein  for his anhattan pera ompany as a replacement for the great rench singing-actor aurice enaud. e sang with the anhattan company in 1908-1910, becoming its principal talian baritone, but he never graduated to the rival etropolitan pera.

ammarco next joined the hicagoamp;ndash;hiladelphia opera company. is career there continued smoothly enough until 1913 when he encountered a disapproving ary arden in a hicago production of osca. he soprano requested that he be replaced; but after he named some of his former distinguished and uncomplaining osca partners, notably mmy estinn, the performances proceeded to be given to critical success.

is final operatic appearances were at the eatro di an arlo in aples in 1919.

part from carpia his debut role at ovent arden, he was a famous igoletto, arcello, ermont, enato, nrico and mleto, appearing opposite some of the finest singers of his day. o bel canto specialist, he was at his best in ardent verismo works, creating the roles of erard in mberto iordanoiordanos ndrea hénier in 1896 and ascart in uggiero eoncavalloeoncavallos azà in 1900.

ammarco was active during an era that was thronged with talian baritones of exceptional ability. t was no small achievement for him to carve out a lucrative international career in the face of powerful competition from the likes of attia attistini, ntonio agini-oletti, iuseppe ampanari, ario ncona, iuseppe acini, ntonio cotti, ugenio iraldoni, iccardo tracciari, itta uffo, omenico iglione orghese, asquale mato and arlo aleffi.

e taught singing after retiring from the stage and died in ilan.

ecordings
ammarco possessed a strong voice with a powerful upper register; but of all the celebrated singers preserved on early recordings, ammarcos are regarded as the most disappointing. he technical quality of his singing disappoints and the timbre of his voice can sound rough; at best he is merely dull. n record, according to cott and teane, he has a singular inability to sing less than mezzo forte and has no concept of legato. e impresses most when delivering declamatory passages in verismo operas see cott, cited below including an early celebrated or notorious recording with the soprano mma arelli from osca, complete with peals of laughter; even in these quot;specialistquot; roles, his singing is unimaginative and crude. any of the depressingly numerous 78-rpm gramophone records that he made prior to orld ar  for the onotipia, ictor and athé companies—and for the forerunner of —are now available on  reissues from various labels.

he olonial, also known as the olonial xpress, was a service of the ennsylvania ailroad and ew ork, ew aven and artford ailroad between nion tation nion tation in ashington,  and outh tation ostonouth tation in oston, assachusetts. t was operated until 1973 by mtrak.

istory
he olonial began on anuary 18, 1892, as a daytime express service between oston and ashington. rom oston, the train traveled west over the ew ork, ew aven amp; artfords hore ine and then the ew ochelle branch to the arlem iver. here, passengers boarded the passenger steamer aryland, which carried them to ersey ity, ew ersey. t that time the ennsylvania ailroad  had no station in anhattan, so passengers heading for ew ork ityew ork traveled to ersey ity, then transferred to anhattan-bound ferries. assengers continuing south on the olonial boarded a new train in ersey ity, which used the ennsylvania main line to reach hiladelphia, ennsylvania, altimore, aryland and ashington.lt;refgt;cite news  titlehe olonial xpress ame and oute of the ew rain hich oes on onday  dateanuary 14, 1892  accessdate2009-12-18  newspaperhe ay ew ondonhe ay  urlhttps//news.google.com/newspapersidn_gamp;sjid6amp;pg3183,906859amp;dqpennsylvania+railroad+colonialamp;hlenlt;/refgt; he train was renamed ederal xpress trainederal xpress in 1894.

n the early 1910s the waterborne segment was dropped; instead, the oston train ran into rand entral erminal, while the ashington train terminated at ennsylvania tation ew ork ityenn tation, which had opened in 1910. assengers used ground transport to move between the two stations, which were a little over a mile apart. n 1917 the opening of the ell ate ridge, which linked the ronx and ueens, ew orkueens and linked the  and the ew aven, allowed trains to run directly through enn tation.lt;ref namequot;lynchquot;gt;ynch-ew aven passenger  page29lt;/refgt;

he  merged into enn entral ransportation in 1968, which absorbed the amp; in 1969. hen mtrak began operations on ay 1, 1971, it took over the ederal, which ran as trains 170 and 171 changed to 173 and 174 in the ovember 14 timetable. ts last trip was made on pril 28, 1973.

mtrak reused the name in 1976 for a new oston–ewport ews, irginiaewport ews train, the olonial mtrak trainolonial, which replaced the ewport ews section of the ames hitcomb iley trainames hitcomb iley.

n 1987, atlett directed a production of an oggins unsense after meeting with oggin and discussing the character of ister ary egina.lt;ref namequot;sentinelquot;/gt; t was staged at the ark wo inner heatre in rlando, lorida. atlett decided to play ister ary as well, taking on a dual role as both director and performer. he was partially inspired to direct the show after witnessing directors unfair treatment of her castmates in previous productions. he said, quot; have worked with many directors who were tyrannical. ou get afraid to do anything because hell yell, ont do that! t makes you crazy...as a director  believe that there can be a democracy.quot;lt;ref namequot;sentinelquot;/gt;

n 1998, atlett was cast as the voice of rs. uff, one of the main characters of ickelodeons animated series pongeob quareants. he is one of the shows nine main cast members and has performed in every season, as well as in all of the ist of pongeob quareants filmstheatrical pongeob films.lt;ref namequot;scottquot;gt;cite weburlhttps//www.nytimes.com/2004/11/19/movies/absorbency-plus-frivolity-a-blend-the-world-needs.htmltitlebsorbency lus rivolity, a lend the orld eedsworkhe ew ork imeslastcottfirst. .dateovember 19, 2004lt;/refgt; tephen illenburg, the creator of the cartoon, specifically sought out atlett to voice rs. uff. e had seen her perform on stage and had a strong vision for rs. uff as a character. atlett quickly accepted and attended early practice sessions with the rest of the voice cast. er first official recording as rs. uff took place on ugust 24, 1998; she recorded dialogue with om enny pongeob and ill agerbakke atrick in a single booth at ickelodeon nimation tudio.

n 2001, atlett was nominated for an nnie ward for her voice-over work as rs. uff, placing in the category quot;est oice cting by a emale erformer in an nimated roduction.quot;lt;refgt;cite webtitle29th nnual nnie ward ominees and inners 2001urlhttp//annieawards.org/29th-annie-awardsworknnie wardpublisher-ollywoodaccessdateuly 4, 2016year2001authortaffarchiveurlhttps//web.archive.org/web/20130102052242/http//annieawards.org/29th-annie-awardsarchivedateanuary 2, 2013lt;/refgt; om enny voice of the title character was also nominated in the same year, making atlett and enny the first two pongeob cast members to be nominated for an award.

s of 2019, voicing rs. uff is atletts only main role on television. atlett described herself as quot;basically retiredquot; in 2013, since she is good friends with the other pongeob cast members, making the pongeob recording booth an easy environment that requires less preparation than in-person performances.lt;refgt;cite newsurlhttps//www.washingtonpost.com/remember-the-time-when-washington-saved-hello-dolly/2013/03/08/7061ad28-85c1-11e2-a80b-3edc779b676f_story.htmltitleemember the time when ashington saved ello, olly!workhe ashington ostpublishereff ezoslastressleyfirstelsondatearch 8, 2013lt;/refgt; bout.comhe bout roups ancy asille noted in 2016 that atletts quot;rich, low tones as teacher rs. uff recall other roles she has had,quot; citing iffrent trokes and *** as programs on which she had used a similar voice.lt;ref namequot;aboutgroupquot;gt;cite weburlhttp//animatedtv.about.com/od/spongebobsquarepants/tp/pongeob-quareants-ast.htmtitlepongeob quareants ast ho oes hat oiceworkbout.comlastasilefirstancydateanuary 30, 2016lt;/refgt;

 remarks  


irdife nternational formerly the nternational ouncil for ird reservation  is a global partnership of onservation movementconservation organisations that strives to conserve birds, their habitats, and global biodiversity, working with people towards sustainability in the use of natural resources. t is the worlds largest partnership of conservation organisations, with over 120 partner organisations.lt;refgt;cite webtitleirdife artnersurlhttp//www.birdlife.org/worldwide/partnership/birdlife-partnerspublisherirdife nternationalaccessdate30 ugust 2015lt;/refgt;

t has a membership of more than 2.5 million people and partner organizations in more than 100 countries. ajor partners include oyal ociety for the rotection of irds, the ild ird ociety of apan, and the ational udubon ociety.. ational udubon ociety. he groups headquarters are located in ambridgeambridge, .

irdife nternationals priorities include preventing extinction of bird species, identifying and safeguarding important sites for birds, maintaining and restoring key bird habitats, and empowering conservationists worldwide. uided by a global council, member organizations implement the groups strategies on local, regional, and national levels.

irdife nternational has identified 7,500 important bird areas and manages more than 2,500,000 million acres 1,000,000 hectares of wildlife habitat. s the official listing authority for birds for the nternational nion for onservation of atureorld onservation nion’s  ed isted ist of threatened species, irdife nternational has identified more than 1,000 bird species threatened with extinction and has developed conservation strategies for each of them.lt;refgt;ite weburlhttps//www.iucn.org/theme/species/our-work/birdstitleed ist uthority for birdslt;/refgt;

istory
ile warden a igue eychelles 1970s.jpgthumbright warden with a  mark on his uniform on a igue, eychelles in the 1970s
irdife nternational is a worldwide alliance of nongovernmental organizations that promotes the conservation of birds and their habitats. irdife nternational was founded in 1922 as the nternational ouncil for ird reservation by merican ornithologists . ilbert earson and ean heodore elacour under the name nternational ommittee for ird rotection. he group was renamed nternational ommittee for ird reservation in 1928, nternational ouncil for ird reservation in 1960, and quot;irdife nternationalquot; in 1993.lt;refgt;cite webtitleur istoryurlhttp//www.birdlife.org/worldwide/partnership/our-historypublisherirdife nternationalaccessdate30 ugust 2015lt;/refgt;

egional work
irdife nternational has conservation work programmes in the following parts of the world, which it describes as quot;regionsquot;lt;refgt;cite webtitleegionsurlhttp//www.birdlife.org/regionspublisherirdife nternationalaccessdate30 ugust 2015lt;/refgt;—frica,lt;refgt;cite webtitlefricaurlhttp//www.birdlife.org/africapublisherirdife nternationalaccessdate30 ugust 2015lt;/refgt; the mericas,lt;refgt;cite webtitlemericasurlhttp//www.birdlife.org/americaspublisherirdife nternationalaccessdate30 ugust 2015lt;/refgt; sia,lt;refgt;cite webtitlesiaurlhttp//www.birdlife.org/asiapublisherirdife nternationalaccessdate30 ugust 2015lt;/refgt; urope and entral sia,lt;refgt;cite webtitleurope and entral siaurlhttp//www.birdlife.org/europe-and-central-asiapublisherirdife nternationalaccessdate30 ugust 2015lt;/refgt; the iddle astlt;refgt;cite webtitleiddle asturlhttp//www.birdlife.org/middle-eastpublisherirdife nternationalaccessdate30 ugust 2015lt;/refgt; and the acific.lt;refgt;cite webtitleacificurlhttp//www.birdlife.org/pacificpublisherirdife nternationalaccessdate30 ugust 2015lt;/refgt;

ed ist

n her youth hristians only aspiration was to become a physician.lt;ref nameparla36gt;#arlaarla, p. 36.lt;/refgt; fter she graduated from secondary school she had a fortuitous meeting with her screen idol rrol lynn, who became her lover, and she was persuaded by him to give up her hopes of joining the medical profession, move to ollywood, and pursue an acting career.lt;ref nameparla36/gt; ot long after arriving in ollywood she was spotted by ouis . ayers secretary at a fashion show in everly ills. e offered, and she accepted, a seven-year contract with .lt;ref nameparla37gt;#arlaarla, p. 37.lt;/refgt;

er stage name was invented by lynn, who gave her the surname of letcher hristian of utiny on the ounty fame. lynn had played letcher hristian in a 1933 ustralian film.lt;refgt;homas culty 2004 rrol lynn he ife and areer, carland, pp. 165, 166, 0786417501.lt;/refgt;

n his autobiography, y icked, icked ays,lt;refgt;rrol lynn 2002 y icked, icked aysquot;, owman amp; ittlefield, 978-0815412502lt;/refgt; lynn states that immediately after inda hristians screen test, he offered to pay for her to have a couple of crooked teeth fixed. hen he got a whopping bill, he discovered that she had taken the opportunity to undergo major cosmetic dentistry. ears later, when he met her again, he said, quot;mile, baby –  want to see those choppers they took their first bite out of me.quot;

he made her film debut in the 1944 musical comedy p in rms, co-starring anny aye and inah hore. his movie also happened to be anny ayes own first film.lt;ref nameparla37/gt; his film was followed by oliday in exico 1946, reen olphin treet filmreen olphin treet 1947, and what was perhaps her best-known film, arzan and the ermaidslt;ref nameparla37/gt; 1948. he was the subject of a well-known photograph published in the anuary 1, 1949, issue of ogue magazineogue.

hristian was the first ond girl to appear on screen, playing alerie athis opposite arry elson as ames ond in the 1954  adaptation of asino oyale limax!asino oyale, beating rsula ndress to the screen by eight years.

n 2001, a olden alm tar on the alm prings, alifornia, alm prings alk of tarsalk of tars was dedicated to her.lt;refgt;cite weburlhttp//www.palmspringswalkofstars.com/web-storage/tars/tars%20dedicated%20by%20date.pdf format titlealm prings alk of tars by date dedicated websitepalmspringswalkofstars.com url-statusdead archiveurlhttps//web.archive.org/web/20121013165655/http//www.palmspringswalkofstars.com/web-storage/tars/tars%20dedicated%20by%20date.pdf archivedate2012-10-13 lt;/refgt;

hristians fame, however, was largely derived from having been married to and divorced from the popular screen idol yrone owerlt;ref nameparla35/gt; 1949–56. he couple married in ome, taly, at anta rancesca omana, omeanta rancesca omana church; hristian wore a formfitting gold-damask gown, and the church was decorated with two thousand sther carnations.lt;refgt;cite weburlhttp//tyforum.bravepages.com/artc/oggi-2-3-49.htmltitleagazine rticles - atrimonio in echnicolorpublisherlt;/refgt; he and ower were the parents of singer omina ower and actress aryn ower.lt;ref nameparla39gt;#arlaarla, p. 39.lt;/refgt; omina was one half of the talian singing duo l ano and omina ower.

 month after she divorced yrone ower, hristian was seen with panish racing driver lfonso de ortago, who was married to merican arroll de ortago later arroll etrie. arroll had recently given birth to quot;onsquot; second child nthony. e ortago was also dating model orian eigh, mother of his recently born illegitimate son im. inda was photographed with de ortago at the 1957 ille iglia car race. he photo shows hristian leaning in to kiss on before he drove off and crashed his errari, killing himself, his navigator d elson and at least ten spectators in the process. he press labeled the photo quot;he iss of eathquot;. e ortago was 28 years old. er ex-husband, yrone ower, died the following year of a heart attack at the age of 44. hristian was later married to the ome-based ritish actor dmund urdom.lt;ref nameobit/gt;

n several occasions hristian and ower were offered the opportunity to work together, but for various reasons each offer was refused or rescinded.lt;ref nameparla39/gt; he most notable opportunity to co-star together came in 1953, when they were offered leading roles in rom ere to ternity. ower did not want to do the filmlt;ref nameparla39/gt; and rejected the offer. he roles went to onna eed and ontgomery lift. 

hristian had a relationship with lenn ord in the early 1960s.lt;refgt;ord, eter. lenn ord  ife isconsin ilm tudies. adison, isconsin niversity of isconsin ress, 2011. p.209 978-0-29928-154-0lt;/refgt;

he entucky ardinal was a nightly convert312mileadjon passenger train operated by mtrak from 1999 to 2003 between hicago, llinois, and ouisville, entucky, via ndianapolis, ndiana. n the three days that the ardinal passenger trainardinal ran, the entucky ardinal operated as a section, splitting at ndianapolis. n the other four days, it ran on its own to hicago.

istory
ilei-evel coach and express boxcar on the entucky ardinal at effersonville, ugust 2001.jpgthumbleft typical entucky ardinal consist a 32-8 locomotive out of frame, a 42 locomotive, a i-evel coach, and a boxcar
ileentucky ardinal at ouisville, ay 2002.jpgthumblefthe entucky ardinal at ouisville in ay 2002
etween ay 1971–ugust 1974 mtraks loridian trainloridian ran from hicago to lorida via ndianapolis and ouisville. ue to poor track conditions on the enn entral trackage in ndiana, the train was rerouted to the west north of ashville, ennessee. n pril 1975 the train was routed back east over the former onon ailroad, again serving ouisville, but bypassing ndianapolis to the west. he loridian served ouisville until its discontinuance in ctober 1979.lt;refgt;arvnbanders2006pp80–83lt;/refgt;

n ecember 17, 1999, the entucky ardinal started running as an extension of the oosier tate passenger trainoosier tate, which ran four days a week between hicago and ndianapolis filling in the gaps in the ardinal schedule. he entucky ardinal ran as trains 850 southbound and 851 northbound, the same numbers as the oosier tate. he train, operated along trackage that had last been used by the loridian mtrakloridian in 1974, was an attempt to attract express business from nited arcel ervice, which maintains its air-express hub at ouisville nternational irport. t first the train only ran from ndianapolis south to effersonville, ndiana, a ouisville suburb, where a new mtrak ail and xpress facility was built. he city of ouisville spent $370,000 in 2001 to renovate its nion tation ouisvillenion tation for the service, and on ecember 4 the entucky ardinal started to use a new track on the west side of the nion tation parking lot, marking mtraks return to ouisville after a 20-year absence.

nlike its predecessor, the entucky ardinal was a full-fledged daily train. n the days the ardinal operated, the southbound entucky ardinal split from the eastbound ardinal train 50 at ndianapolis and continued to ouisville, while the northbound entucky ardinal combined with the westbound ardinal train 51 for the journey to hicago.

he train was handicapped by inconvenient departure and arrival times and slow travel times, especially on the segment from ndianapolis south to ouisville. his segment was operated over the ouisville and ndiana ailroad, which had purchased the line from onrail in 1994, and had a speed limit of 30 miles per hour 48amp;nbsp;km/h over most of the route due to its jointed rail. his made travel on the southern leg of the entucky ardinal slower than automobile traffic on the parallel nterstate 65.

ith the opening in 1999, reyhound inesreyhound began running hruway otorcoach bus connections from effersonville south to ashville, ennessee, with stops at lizabethtown lizabethtown and owling reen, entucky. hough rail passenger advocates tried to get the trains route extended to ashville in an effort to increase ridership, mtrak lost its mail contract, and the entucky ardinal last ran uly 4, 2003, restoring the old oosier tate on uly 6 the ardinal ran both ways on uly 5.

saiah homas anuary 19, 1749 – pril 4, 1831 was an merican istory of merican newspapersnewspaper publisher and author. e performed the first public reading of the nited tates eclaration of ndependenceeclaration of ndependence in orcester, assachusetts, and reported the first account of the attles of exington and oncord.  e was the founder of the merican ntiquarian ociety.

iography

arly life and career
homas was born in oston, assachusetts. e was apprenticed on uly 7, 1756, to echariah owle, a oston printer, with whom, after working as a printer in ity of alifaxalifax, ortsmouth, ew ampshireortsmouth ew ampshire and harleston, outh arolinaharleston outh arolina, he formed a partnership in 1770.lt;refgt;rom olonial imes to the resent. eraldine oucha. ew ork. cribner. 1995.lt;/refgt;

he assachusetts py
mageassachusetts py 3a10607u.pngthumbasthead ritish publishingasthead of uly 7, 1774 issue

he partnership was formed to publish the assachusetts py, and lasted for three months, after which homas continued publication alone. or the papers motto, he chose quot;pen to all parties, but influenced by none.quot;lt;ref nameacabgt;ppletonswstitlehomas, saiahyear1900inline1lt;/refgt;  nitially it came out three times each week, then under his sole ownership as a semi-weekly, and beginning in 1771, as a weekly. he paper soon espoused the hig cause and was the object of government efforts to suppress it.sfnhisholm1911 n 1771 ov. homas utchinson governorhomas utchinson ordered the attorney general to prosecute homas, but the grand jury failed to find cause for indictment.lt;ref nameacab/gt;

n oston, in 1774, homas published the oyal merican agazine, which was continued for a short time by oseph reenleaf, and which contained many engravings by aul evere.sfnhisholm1911

scape to orcester
ary of the ories growing resentment of the independence of the py, on pril 16, 1775 three days before the attle of oncord, in which he took part, homas took his presses from oston and set them up in orcester, assachusettsorcester. is other property was destroyed.lt;ref nameacab/gt;  n orcester, he published and sold books, built a paper mill and bindery, and continued the paper until 1802 save for gaps in 1776–1778 and in 1786–1788. he py supported eorge ashington and the ederalist arty. e was also postmaster for a time.

homas married ary owle, described as a quot;half-cousinquot;, on ay 26, 1779.lt;refgt;ouglas rawford curtriecurtrie, ouglas . he ook he tory of rinting amp; ookmaking. ew ork xford niversity ress, 1943 431.lt;/refgt; round 1802, homas gave his orcester business over to his son, including the control of the py.sfnhisholm1911

ater life
rom 1775 until 1803, homas published the ew ngland lmanac, continued until 1819 by his son, saiah homas, r. t had something of the flavor of enjamin ranklins oor ichards lmanac.lt;ref nameacab/gt; n 1786 he procured from urope the first font of music type that was brought to the nited tates, and he was the first printer in the .. to use such type. e was engaged at alpole, ew ampshire, in book publishing and printing the armers useum, and in 1788 opened a bookstore in oston under the firm name of homas and ndrews, also establishing branches of his publishing business in several parts of the nited tates. he monthly assachusetts agazine was published by the firm, with benezer . ndrews, in eight volumes, from 1789 until 1796. t orcester he printed a folio edition of the ible in 1791, saac attsatts salms and ymns, and most of the ibles and school books that were used in the .. at that date.lt;ref nameacab/gt;sfnhisholm1911

is ambition throughout his life was to write an extensive book on the history of publishing.
e began what would become istory of rinting in merica bookistory of rinting in merica in 1808.lt;ref namecurtrie432gt;ouglas rawford curtriecurtrie, ouglas . he ook he tory of rinting amp; ookmaking. ew ork xford niversity ress, 1943 432.lt;/refgt; ully titled istory of rinting in merica, with a iography of rinters, and an ccount of ewspapers, it was published in two volumes in 1810.  second edition, published in 1874, was prepared by his grandson enjamin ranklin homas and included a catalog of merican publications previous to 1776 and a memoir of saiah homas.

n ovember 1812, homas founded the merican ociety of ntiquaries, now known as the merican ntiquarian ociety, partly to take care of the extensive library he had accumulated in preparing his history of publishing. t its first meeting, homas was elected president, a role he held until his death.lt;ref namecurtrie432/gt; n addition to nearly 8,000 volumes from his collection, he gave to its library tracts, and one of the most valuable files of newspapers in the country, and he presented land and a hall, with a provision equal to $24,000 for its maintenance.lt;ref nameacab/gt;

homas spent his final days in orcester. pon his death in 1831, he bequeathed his entire library, his collection of early merican newspapers, as well as his personal papers and records to the merican ntiquarian ociety.lt;ref namecurtrie432/gt;

homas is interred at ural emetery orcester, assachusettsural emetery in orcester.lt;refgt;https//www.bostonglobe.com/sports/2016/04/27/remembering-original-isaiah-thomas-patriot-not-celtic/7uu1uibv34fbf4/story.html oston lobelt;/refgt;

egacy
homass grandson enjamin homas congressman. . homas noted his grandfathers importance in founding the merican ntiquarian ociety. quot;e saw and understood, no man better, from what infinitely varied and minute sources the history of a nations life was to be drawn; that the only safe rule was to gather up all the fragments so that nothing be lost.quot;lt;refgt;ouglas rawford curtriecurtrie, ouglas . he ook he tory of rinting amp; ookmaking. ew ork xford niversity ress, 1943 434.lt;/refgt; n 1943, ublishers eekly created the arey-homas ward for creative publishing, naming it honor of athew arey and saiah homas.lt;refgt;http//www.time.com/time/magazine/article/0,9171,774310,00.html quot;ublishers scarquot;; ime, ebruary 15, 1943lt;/refgt;

rudence nne illiers arrow runs born anuary 20, 1948 is an merican author, meditation teacher, and film producer. he is the daughter of film director ohn arrow and actress aureen ullivan and younger sister of actress ia arrow.lt;ref namequot;op istoryquot;/gt; he is the subject of the he eatleseatles song quot;ear rudencequot;.lt;refgt;cite weburlhttp//www.pophistorydig.com/tagbeatles-prudence-farrowtitle ear rudence, 1967-1968firstacklastoylepublisheropistoryig.comdateuly 27, 2009accessdateay 15, 2010lt;/refgt;

arly life
arrow was raised in the atholic faith and attended convent schools. he learned the ranscendental editation technique  in 1966 at  and next year became interested in yoga, opening a yoga institute at a former church in oston.lt;ref namegt;cite newstitleear rudence living, teaching  in altonworkorthwest lorida aily ewslocationort alton each, la.date ctober 25, 1992page1lt;/refgt;lt;refgt;cite news work he ydney orning erald dateovember 9, 1967 url https//news.google.com/newspapersidpamp;sjidcamp;pg1360,2696923amp;dqprudence+farrowamp;hlendepartmentomens ection page8 title rt and fashion on showlt;/refgt;lt;ref namequot;irlquot;gt;cite newstitleirl efects rom onventdatectober 24, 1967agencyssociated ressworkettysburg imespage5url https//news.google.com/newspapersidq2wmamp;sjidl8amp;pg902,610517amp;dqprudence+farrowamp;hlen lt;/refgt; n 1968 arrow, along with her sister ia and brother atrick, traveled with aharishi ahesh ogi from ew ork ityew ork to ndia,lt;refgt;ould, onathan 2007 armony ooks, ant uy e ove he eatles, ritain, and merica, 978-0-307-35337-5lt;/refgt; and then to the aharishis ashram in ishikesh for a ranscendental editation teacher training course.lt;ref namequot;op istoryquot;gt;quot;lthough the eatles left the retreat before the course on transcendental meditation was finished, rudence arrow, ike ove of the each oys, and others stayed on and became  teachersquot;lt;/refgt;

he eatles at ishikeshhe eatles arrived shortly thereafter.lt;refgt;he ltimate eatles uiz ook, ichael ockinson, page 128, t. artins ress, 1990.lt;/refgt; arrow was dedicated to practicing the  technique so she could become a  teacher. he said quot; would always rush straight back to my room after lectures and meals so  could meditate. ohn ennonohn, eorge arrisoneorge and aul cartneyaul would all want to sit around jamming and having a good time and d be flying into my room. hey were all serious about what they were doing, but they just werent as fanatical as mequot;.lt;ref namequot;op istoryquot;/gt; he quot;turned into a near reclusequot; and quot;rarely came outquot; of her cottage.lt;refgt;cite newstitle   arrow tells story of ear rudence ister meditated 23 hours a day, oblivious to song written for herfirstlastworkilwaukee ournal entineldateovember 5, 1995page8lt;/refgt; ennon was asked to quot;contact her and make sure she came out more often to socializequot; and he wrote the song quot;ear rudencequot;. ccording to ennon,  quot;hed been locked in for three weeks and was trying to reach od quicker than anyone elsequot;.lt;ref namequot;op istoryquot;/gt;lt;ref namequot;he eadquot;gt;he merican book of the ead, liver rager, page 90, imon and chuster, 1997lt;/refgt;

areer
arrow taught  for several decades after her teacher training course in ndia.lt;ref namequot;op istoryquot;/gt;lt;refgt;ere, here and verywhere the 100 best eatles songs, tephen  pignesi, ichael ewis, page 252lt;/refgt; mong those she mentored was comedian ndy aufman.lt;refgt;ite book publisher  elacorte ress last  ehme first  ill title  ost in the funhouse date  1999-12-01page97lt;/refgt; he returned to ndia for further instruction from the aharishi in 1986lt;ref name/gt; and has taught ranscendental editation in lorida since 1970.lt;ref nameautogenerated1gt;http//www.tm.org/local_teachers/northeastflorida.html /  lorida  program web sitelt;/refgt;

his is a list of famous or important aroese people. n a small island-society of fewer than 50,000 inhabitants, each person can gain certain meaning for the entire nation. he people listed below, are among those who played or play a distinct role in aroese culture, politics and history. any of them are renowned outside the aroes, especially in enmark and other ordic countries.

ersonal life

 name  ellow mongoose
 status  
 status_system  3.1
 status_ref  lt;ref nameiucngt;cite iucn titleynictis penicillata author1o inh an, . author2avallini, . author3aylor, . last-author-ampyes year2015 pagee.4159745205726lt;/refgt;
 image  ynictis penicillata tosha, 2011.jpg
 genus  ynictis
 parent_authority  illiam gilbygilby, 1833
 species  penicillata
 authority  eorges uvieruvier, 1829
 range_map  ellow ongoose area.png
 range_map_caption  ellow mongoose range


he yellow mongoose ynictis penicillata, sometimes referred to as the red meerkat, is a member of the mongoose family. t averages about 1amp;nbsp;lb 1/2amp;nbsp;kg in weight and about 20 in 500amp;nbsp;mm in length. t lives in open country, from semi-desert scrubland to grasslands in ngola, otswana, outh frica, amibia, and imbabwe. 
ileellow ongoose lipriviersberg ohannesburg.jpgthumbnailellow mongoose in lipriviersberg, ohannesburg

axonomy
ynictis penicillata is the onotypic taxononly member of its genus, but as many as twelve subspecies of yellow mongoose have been described.lt;ref name  3gt;3 arnivora id14000508 page564 headingpecies ynictis penicillatalt;/refgt;
 haracteristics 
n general, the yellow mongoose has lighter highlights on the underbelly and chin, a bushy tail, and a complete lack of sexual dimorphism. outhern yellow mongooses are larger, have yellow or reddish fur, longer fur, and a longer tail with a characteristic white tip. orthern subspecies tend towards smaller size, grey colouration, a grey or darker grey tip to the tail, and shorter hair more appropriate to the hotter climate.

ehaviour and ecology
ileuchsmanguste 2.jpgthumbellow mongoose
he yellow mongoose is primarily diurnal animaldiurnal, though nocturnal activity has been observed. iving in colonies of up to 20 individuals in a permanent burrow complex, the yellow mongoose will often co-exist with ape ground squirrels or suricates and share maintenance of the warren, adding new tunnels and burrows as necessary. he tunnel system has many entrances, nearby which the yellow mongoose makes its latrine animallatrines.

he yellow mongoose is a carnivore, feeding mostly on termites, grasshoppers and crickets, but also on rodents and small birds. n urban environments in outh frica, it also forages among human food garbage.lt;refgt;ite journal lastronk first. last2illay first2. date2019 titlelexible se of rban esources by the ellow ongoose ynictis penicillata journalnimals volume9 issue7 pages447  doi10.3390/ani9070447lt;/refgt;

ocial structure
ileynictis penicillata, ake istrict ildlife ark.jpgthumb yellow mongoose in ake istrict ildlife ark, umbria, northwestern ngland
he resocialitysocial structure of the yellow mongoose is hierarchyhierarchical, based around a central breeding pair and their most recent offspring. here are also subadults, the elderly, or adult relatives of the central pair. ale ranges tend to overlap, while females from other dens have contiguous non-overlapping ranges. very day, the alpha male will mark members of his group with anal gland secretions, and his boundaries with facial and anal secretions, as well as urine. he alpha male also rubs his back against raised objects, leaving behind hair as a visual territorial markingmarker of territory. ther members of the group mark their dens with cheek secretions.  colony can have 20-40 members.

redators
redators of the yellow mongoose are birds of prey, snakes and jackals. hen frightened, the yellow mongoose will growl and secrete from its anal glands. t can also scream, bark, and purr, though these are exceptions, as the yellow mongoose is usually silent, and communicates mood and status through tail movements.

eproduction
ileynictis_penicillata_mating2.jpgthumbellow mongooses mating
he yellow mongooses mating season is between uly and eptember, and it gives birth underground between ctober and ecember, with no bedding material, in a clean chamber of the burrow system. sually, two offspring are produced per pregnancy, and they are weaned at 10 weeks, reaching adult size after 10 months.

abies
here is some concern about the yellow mongooses role as a natural reservoir of rabies. ost frican wild animals die within several weeks of infection with rabies, but it seems that certain genetic strains of the yellow mongoose can carry it asymptomatically, but infectiously, for years.lt;refgt;cite journal authoraylor, .. title systematic and population genetic approach to the rabies problem in the yellow mongoose ynictis penicillata journalnderstepoort ournal of eterinary esearch volume60 issue4 pages379–387 date1993 pmid7777324 urlhttps//repository.up.ac.za/bitstream/handle/2263/33125/54taylor1993.pdfsequence1amp;isllowedylt;/refgt;

irborne anger is an action game developed and published by icrorose for the mstrad , ommodore 64,  pectrum, and  in 1987, and ported to the miga and tari  by magitec esign in 1989. n the game, a sole nited tates rmy angers.. rmy anger is sent to infiltrate the enemy territory to complete various objectives. he game was followed by pecial orces video gamepecial orces in 1991.

ameplay
he game consists of several missions, in which the player controls a sole anger whose objectives include capturing an enemy officer, destroying an enemy bunker, taking out a urface-to-air missile site, and rescuing a captured , which would possibly free a roster member that was labeled ... he game creates the maps and objective locations randomly, so the player is required to plan each mission carefully, because no mission is the same.

t the start of each mission, the player is presented with a short overview of the mission, and can select a anger from a roster of available soldiers. he player is then in control of an aircraft, described as a ell-oeing -22 sprey-22 sprey and is allowed to drop three ammunitionammo crates over the enemy territory. nce the three containers are dropped, the anger is parachuted into the area. pon touch-down, the player has to overcome several obstacles, including enemy soldiers and officers, land minemine fields, efensive fighting positionfoxholes and bunkers. ue to limited ammunition, the player needs to plan his path through the territory. he dropped ammo crates provide the soldier with fresh hand grenades and ammo. fter completing the mission, the anger has to navigate to a pick-up point within a time limit. f the anger is captured but not killed, the player can start an optional rescue mission using another soldier from the roster. ach successful mission increases the rank of the individual anger, up to colonel.

eception

ile .thumbrightwo missionaries of he hurch of esus-hrist of atter-day aints

issionaries of he hurch of esus hrist of atter-day aints  hurch—widely known as ormon missionaries—are volunteer representatives of the he hurch of esus hrist of atter-day aints hurch who engage variously in roselytismproselytizing, church service, humanitarian aid, and community service. ormon missionaries may serve on a full- or part-time basis, depending on the assignment, and are organized geographically into ission  hurchmissions. he mission assignment could be to any one of the ist of missions of he hurch of esus hrist of atter-day aints407lt;ref namequot;tatistics 2016quot;gt;cite press releasetitle2016 tatistical eport for 2017 pril eneral onferenceurlhttps//newsroom.churchofjesuschrist.org/article/2015-statistical-report-april-2016-general-conferencewebsiteormonewsroom.orgpublisherhe hurch of esus hrist of atter-day aintsdatepril 1, 2017accessdateecember 24, 2017lt;/refgt; missions organized worldwide.

he  hurch is one of the most active modern practitioners of missionary work, reporting that it had more than 70,000 full-time missionaries worldwide at the end of 2016lt;ref namequot;tatistics 2016quot; /gt; as well as more than 33,000 part-time church-service missionaries.lt;ref namequot;tatistics 2016quot; /gt;  ost full-time  missionaries are single young men and women in their late teens and early twenties and older couples no longer with children in their home. issionaries are often assigned to serve far from their homes, including in other countries. any missionaries learn a new language at a missionary training center as part of their assignment. issions typically last two years for males, 18 months for females, and 1 to 3 years for older couples. he  hurch strongly encourages, but does not require, missionary service for young men. ll ormon missionaries serve voluntarily and do not receive a salary for their work; they typically finance missions themselves or with assistance from family or other church members. any atter-day aints save money during their teenage years to cover their mission expenses.

hroughout the istory of he hurch of esus hrist of atter-day aintschurchs history, over one million missionaries have been sent on missions.lt;ref name  onemillion1gt;citation url https//newsroom.churchofjesuschrist.org/article/one-million-missionaries-thirteen-million-members title ews tory ndash ne illion issionaries, hirteen illion embers work ewsroom publisher  hurch date une 25, 2007 accessdate 2012-11-27 lt;/refgt;lt;ref name  onemillion2gt;citation url http//www.deseretnews.com/article/680194052/1-million-missionaries-for--hurch--so-far.html title 1 million missionaries for  hurch – so far last alch first ad newspaper eseret orning ews date une 26, 2007 accessdate 2012-11-27 lt;/refgt;

reparation to serve
ignificance and basic qualifications
 hurch resident of the hurch  hurchpresident pencer . imball said, quot;very young man should fill a missionquot;.lt;ref namekimballgt;cite newslastimballfirstpencer .authorlinkpencer . imballtitlehen the orld ill e onvertedurlhttps//www.churchofjesuschrist.org/study/ensign/1974/10/when-the-world-will-be-convertedlangengmagazinensign  magazinensigndatectober 3, 1974accessdateovember 27, 2012lt;/refgt; ompleting a mission is often described as a rite of passage for a young atter-day aint.lt;refgt;citation first ary last hepherd first2 ordon last2 hepherd year 1998 title ormon assage  issionary hronicle location rbana publisher niversity of llinois ress isbn 0-252-06662-6 pages 19–34.lt;/refgt;lt;ref namemetamorphosisgt;cite newslastletcher tackfirsteggyauthorlinkeggy letcher tacktitleission metamorphosisurlhttp//archive.sltrib.com/article.phpid6262037amp;itypenewspaperhe alt ake ribunedateune 30, 2007accessdateugust 4, 2018lt;/refgt;lt;refgt;cite newslastirkpatrickfirstavid .titleomney, earching and arnest, et is ath in 60surlhttps//www.nytimes.com/2007/11/15/us/politics/15romney.htmlpagewantedallnewspaperhe ew ork imesdateovember 15, 2007accessdateovember 27, 2012archiveurlhttps//web.archive.org/web/20090425165207/http//www.nytimes.com/2007/11/15/us/politics/15romney.htmlpagewantedallarchivedatepril 25, 2009url-statuslivelt;/refgt;lt;refgt;cite book first eith last arry contribution he ormon issionary ompanionship page 182 year 2001 origyear 1994 title ontemporary ormonism ocial cience erspectives editor1-first arie editor1-last ornwall editor1-link arie ornwall editor2-first im . editor2-last eaton editor3-first awrence . editor3-last oung place rbana publisher niversity of llinois ress isbn 0-252-02076-6 oclc 28721262 lt;/refgt; he phrase quot;the best two years of my lifequot; is a common cliché among returned missionaries when describing their experience.lt;refgt;citation last urham first owell ., r. url https//www.churchofjesuschrist.org/study/new-era/1973/06/return-of-the-missionarylangeng title eturn of the issionary journal ew ra magazineew ra dateune 1973 page 54 accessdate 2012-11-27 .lt;/refgt;lt;refgt;citation first anet last righam url https//www.churchofjesuschrist.org/study/ensign/1978/12/when-the-best-two-years-are-overlangeng title hen he est wo ears re ver journal nsign  magazinensign dateecember 1978 page 29 accessdate 2012-11-27 .lt;/refgt; lthough ordon . inckley had suggested that a mission is not to be a rite of passage,lt;refgt;cite newslastauntfirstaenetitleew ission residents ounseled to ove heir issionaries and the eopleurlhttps//www.churchofjesuschrist.org/study/ensign/1990/09/news-of-the-church/new-mission-presidents-counseled-to-love-their-missionaries-and-the-peoplelangengmagazinensign  magazinensigndateeptember 1990lt;/refgt; this cultural aspect remains.citation neededdateecember 2011 ith the usual starting age of 18–20, a mission provides a clear event or marker for the traditional age of adulthood, but is not necessary for continuance in church membership.

oung men between the ages of 18 and 25 who meet standards of worthiness are strongly encouraged to consider a two-year, full-time roselytismproselytizing mission. his expectation is based in part on the ew estament passage quot;o ye therefore, and teach all nationsquot; sible ing ames/atthew#hapter 28att. 28 19–20. he minimum age had previously been age 19 in most countries until ctober 6, 2012, when hurch resident homas . onson announced that all male missionaries, regardless of nation, could serve from age 18.lt;ref namequot;issionarygequot;gt;cite press releasetitlehurch owers issionary ervice geurlhttps//newsroom.churchofjesuschrist.org/article/church-lowers-age-requirement-for-missionary-servicepublisherntellectual eserve, nc.websiteormonewsroom.orgdatectober 6, 2012accessdateugust 4, 2018lt;/refgt;  rior to the announcement, some countries held that male missionaries may be 18 years old because of educational or military requirements.lt;ref nameyoungmissionariesgt;cite newslastletcher tackfirsteggyauthorlinkeggy letcher tacktitleome ormon men can go on missions at age 18urlhttp//www.sltrib.com/sltrib/blogsfaithblog/52458313-180/mormon-mission-age-academy.html.cspnewspaperhe alt ake ribunedateugust 25, 2011archiveurlhttps//web.archive.org/web/20121011082639/http//www.sltrib.com/sltrib/blogsfaithblog/52458313-180/mormon-mission-age-academy.html.csparchivedatectober 11, 2012accessdateovember 27, 2012url-status deaddfmdy-alllt;/refgt;  t was also announced that young women may serve beginning at age 19 instead of 21.lt;ref namequot;issionarygequot; /gt;  n 2007, approximately 30% of all 19-year-old  men became ormon missionaries; from  families that are active in the church, approximately 80–90% of 19-year-old men serve a mission.lt;ref namemetamorphosis/gt;

issionaries can be sent home for violating mission rules, and occasionally missionaries choose to go home for health or various other reasons. owever, the vast majority of missionaries serve the whole two-year men or eighteen-month women terms.citation neededdatectober 2014

s of 2007, 80% of all ormon missionaries were young, single men, 13% were young single women and 7% retired couples.lt;ref name  metamorphosis/gt; omen who would like to serve a mission must meet the same standards of worthiness and be at least 19 years old. omen generally serve as missionaries for 18 months. arried retired couples, on the other hand, are encouraged to serve missions, but their length of service may vary from 6 to 36 months depending on their circumstances and means.lt;ref namechasehallgt;cite newslastallfirsthasetitlehorter stints may draw more senior  missionariesurlhttp//www.sltrib.com/sltrib/lifestyle/51975755-80/church-missionaries-senior-lds.html.cspnewspaperhe alt ake ribunedateune 15, 2011accessdateovember 27, 2012lt;/refgt; ny single retired person may also be called to serve in what is known as senior missionary service. n the last two decades, the  hurch has stepped up its call for senior couple missionaries.

tandards of worthiness
ll missionaries must meet certain minimum standards of worthiness. mong the standards that a prospective missionary must demonstrate adherence to are regular attendance at orship services of he hurch of esus hrist of atter-day aintschurch meetings, regular personal prayer, regular study of the tandard orksscriptures, adherence to the law of chastity sexual purity, adherence to the ord of isdom code of health and nutrition, payment of tithetithing, spiritual diligence and testimony of od.

ther exclusionary factors
n addition to spiritual preparedness, church ishop atter ay aintsbishops are instructed to ensure that prospective missionaries are physically, mentally, and emotionally capable of full-time missionary work. n the same speech where he called for quot;every young manquot; to fill a mission, imball added, quot;we realize that while all men definitely should, all men are not prepared to teach the gospel abroad.quot;lt;ref namekimball /gt; part from general issues of worthiness and ability, there are a number of specific situations that will disqualify a person from becoming a full-time missionary for the  hurch. hose excluded include those who would have to leave dependent children in the care of someone else; young couples who are still of childbearing age; those who are in debt and have not made arrangements to meet these obligations; those who are on legal probation or parole; couples with serious unresolved marital problems; those who are -positive; and those who have been convicted of sexual abuse. dditionally, members who have submitted to, performed, encouraged, paid for, or arranged for an abortion except in the case of rape, incest, or the mothers life is in danger are usually excluded from missionary service, as are members who have fathered or borne a child out of wedlock; men under 26 and women under 40 who have been divorced; and anyone who has participated in homosexual activity after age 16.lt;refgt;cite book title hurch andbook of nstructions, ook 1 take residencies and ishoprics location alt ake ity publisher  hurch year 2006 pages 92–94 lt;/refgt;

rom the beginnings of the  hurch, people of black frican descent could be members of the church, but up until 1978 the  hurch did not call men of black frican descent to serve on missions, due to the lack people and ormonismban on blacks holding the priesthood. he priesthood ban fficial eclaration—2was lifted during pencer . imballimballs presidency and since 1978 there have been no restrictions to missionary service that are based on race or ethnicity.lt;refgt;citation url https//www.churchofjesuschrist.org/study/manual/gospel-topics-essays/race-and-the-priesthoodlangeng title tudy y opic ospel opics ndash riesthood rdination before 1978 work churchofjesuschrist.org publisher  hurch accessdate 2012-11-27 lt;/refgt;

ission call
fter application to the church and the requisite approval, prospective missionaries receive a quot;call to servequot;—an official notification of their location assignment—from the resident of the hurch  hurchresident of the hurch. he mission call also informs the prospective missionary what language he or she will be expected to use during their mission. embers of the uorum of the welve postles  hurchuorum of the welve postles are responsible for assigning missionaries to a particular mission.  prospective missionary receiving the call to serve is generally considered to be a major event in  culture; family members, friends, and members of the prospective missionarys congregation often gather together when a call arrives, which the prospective missionary opens and reads aloud to the group. ntil 2018, mission calls were mailed to prospective missionaries.  n the summer of 2018, the church announced they would begin emailing mission calls to prospective missionaries. he church began emailing calls to prospective missionaries residing in tah and daho in the summer of 2018, with the goal of expanding to the rest of the nited tates and all countries with reliable internet by the beginning of 2019.lt;refgt;ite weburlhttps//www.churchofjesuschrist.org/church/news/from-snail-mail-to-email-mission-calls-are-going-digitallangengtitlerom quot;nail ailquot; to mail ission alls re oing igital - hurch ews and ventswebsitehurchofesushrist.orgaccess-date2018-10-30lt;/refgt;

emple attendance
efore beginning their mission, prospective male missionaries are usually ordinationordained to the office of an lder ormonismelder in the elchizedek priesthood atter ay aintselchizedek riesthood if they do not hold this office already. ll missionaries are setting apartset apart by the laying on of hands to preach the gospel; this is usually performed by the missionarys stake president. rospective missionaries also usually attend the emple  hurchtemple for the first time to receive their ndowment atter ay aintsendowment if they have not already done so. lt;refgt;ite weburlhttps//www.churchofjesuschrist.org/manual/missionary-preparation-student-manual/chapter-2-personal-worthinesslangengtitlehapter 2 ersonal orthinesswebsitewww.churchofjesuschrist.orgaccess-date2020-03-09lt;/refgt;

raining

ewly called missionaries attend a short training period at one of 15 church issionary raining enters s worldwide.lt;refgt;cite newslastaylorfirstcotttitlehe 14 international issionary raining enters surlhttp//www.deseretnews.com/top/131/0/he-14-international-issionary-raining-enters-s.htmlnewspapereseret ews datearch 23, 2011lt;/refgt; he largest  is located in rovo, tah,lt;refgt;cite webtitlerovo issionary raining enterurlhttps//www.mtc.byu.edu/about/website..edupublisherrigham oung niversityaccessdateugust 4, 2018lt;/refgt; adjacent to righam oung niversity. issionaries who will not be learning a language in order to serve their missions spend three weeks at an  where they practice using proselytizing materials, learn expected conduct, and study the tandard orksscriptures. issionaries bound for foreign-language missions spend six to nine weeks at an , depending on the language to be learned. uring this period, they are encouraged not to speak in their native tongue but rather to immerse themselves in the new language.

issionary conduct
he issionary andbook
he basic standards of missionary service and conduct are contained in the issionary andbook.lt;ref namequot;issionaryandbookquot;gt;cite weburlhttps//www.churchofjesuschrist.org/church/news/changes-to-missionaries-daily-schedule-allows-more-time-to-teach-gospellangengtitleissionary andbookdateuly 7, 2014websitechurchofjesuschrist.orgpublisherntellectual eserve, nc.accessdateugust 4, 2018lt;/refgt; issionaries are instructed that following these standards will protect them both physically and spiritually. ission presidentission presidents have discretion to adjust some of the standards according to local circumstances.lt;ref namequot;issionaryandbookquot;/gt;rp1 he issionary andbook is also commonly and informally referred to as quot;the white handbookquot; or quot;the white biblequot;.lt;refgt;cite newstitleormon missions id you know ... urlhttp//www.sltrib.com/sltrib/news/52648912-78/missionaries-church-lds-missionary.html.csppage2newspaperhe alt ake ribunedateeptember 30, 2011accessdateugust 4, 2018lt;/refgt;

ress and grooming
reviously, full-time  missionaries were required to adhere to a dress code for men, conservative, dark trousers and suit coats, white dress shirts, and conservative ties. or women, modest and professional dresses or blouses and mid-calf length skirts were worn.

n 2013,lt;refgt;ite weburlhttps//www.deseretnews.com/article/865583066/-hurch-tweaks-dress-and-grooming-requirements-for-missionaries.htmltitle hurch tweaks dress and grooming requirements for missionarieslastalkerfirstosephdate2013-07-12websiteeseretews.comlanguageenaccess-date2019-08-05lt;/refgt; the  hurch updated their grooming standards. oung men were no longer required to wear dark suits or a full suit during regular everyday proselytizing activities. hey must, however, remain in professional, conservative attire. or instance, a light colored suit is acceptable. hey are also allowed to wear a sweater or suit vest over their dress shirt and are encouraged to wear colored ties.lt;refgt;cite webtitleissionary ress and roomingurlhttps//www.churchofjesuschrist.org/callings/missionary/dress-groominglangengpublisherntellectual eserve, nc.websitechurchofjesuschrist.orgaccessdatearch 17, 2020lt;/refgt;

ister female missionaries may wear skirts and dresses that cover their knees. oung women are encouraged to dress in colors and patterns, and they may wear appropriate jewelry and accessories.lt;refgt;cite webtitleissionary ress and rooming isters eneral uidelinesurlhttps//www.churchofjesuschrist.org/callings/missionary/dress-groominglangengpublisherntellectual eserve, nc.websitechurchofjesuschrist.orgaccessdatearch 17, 2020lt;/refgt; n 2018 it was announced that female missionaries could wear dress slacks if they wanted, except when attending the temple and during unday worship services, baptismal services, and mission leadership and zone conferences.lt;refgt;https//www.wsbradio.com/news/national/female-mormon-missionaries-given-option-wear-dress-slacks/3vc9x8aa/lt;/refgt;

ileormon missionaries at eotihuacan.jpgleftthumbissionaries in exico, dressed for tropical weatheraltwo young men, the one on the left darker-skinned than the one on the right, who is drinking some orange liquid from a plastic bottle, standing on a stone surface with mountains in the background. hey are both carrying backpacks and wearing white dress shirts, ties and slacks. he one on the right is wearing a short-sleeved shirt and tan slacks
n some areas these standards are altered slightly according to the discretion of the mission president. or example, in hot, humid climates, suit coats are not required, and dress shirts may be short-sleeved. asual clothes may be worn only in limited circumstances, such as when missionaries provide manual labor or exercise.lt;refgt;cite webtitleissionary ress and rooming lders eneral uidelinesurlhttps//missionary.lds.org/clothing/elder/guidelineslangengpublisherntellectual eserve, nc.website.orgaccessdateugust 4, 2018lt;/refgt;

n 2016, the dress guidelines were updated to allow for quot;simple and conservativequot; sunglasses and quot;wide-brimmed hatsquot; as part of a missionarys attire to provide missionaries protection from excessive heat.lt;refgt;cite newslastonesfirstorgantitlepdated  issionary dress and grooming guidelines allow for sunglassesurlhttp//www.deseretnews.com/article/865654548/pdated--missionary-dress-and-grooming-guidelines-allow-for-sunglasses.htmlnewspapereseret ewsdateay 18, 2016accessdateugust 4, 2018lt;/refgt;

ll full-time missionaries wear a name tag that gives their surname with the appropriate title quot;lderquot; or quot;isterquot; in nglish-speaking areas, or their equivalent titles in other languages. he name tag also bears the churchs name, unless the mission president considers this inadvisable due to circumstances in the area e.g., adverse political conditions. issionaries are required to wear the tag at all times in public.

ompanionships
 missionary companionship, consisting of two or occasionally, three missionaries, is the smallest organizational unit of a mission. very missionary is assigned by the mission president to be another missionarys companion. issionary companionships are generally maintained for months at a time and most missionaries will have served with multiple companions by the end of their mission. hese companions very rarely have prior acquaintance outside of the mission. ompanionships are always of the same gender.

issionary companions are instructed to stay together at all times and not to go out of the hearing of their companions voice or out of sight.lt;ref namequot;issionaryandbookquot;/gt;rp30–31 rivacy is allowed only for personal care such as showering. ne of the intentions of this strict policy of staying together is to discourage missionaries from breaking any mission rules.lt;ref namequot;issionaryandbookquot;/gt;rp31 ompanions share the same living quarters and the same bedroom, but not the same bed.lt;ref namequot;issionaryandbookquot;/gt;rp31

hen companions have conflicting personalities or interests, they are encouraged to try to resolve them themselves. f a missionarys companion is having difficulty with the work or with personal problems, missionaries are instructed to give criticism constructively, in private and with respect.lt;ref namequot;issionaryandbookquot;/gt;rp30 n dealing with a problem, missionaries are first to raise the issue with their companion and if it is not resolved, to raise it with the mission president. quot; missionarys first priority is to the ord, then to the mission president and finally to their companionquot;, as the missionary handbook states.lt;ref namequot;issionaryandbookquot;/gt;rp32 igh value is placed on the spiritual commitment to the virtues of humility and love. issionaries are urged to treat the companionship as a relationship that must succeed in being cooperative and selfless, thus improving the spirituality, character and social skills of each individual missionary.

enior couples
enior couples serve as a companionship for the entirety of their mission and have more relaxed rules. nlike single missionaries, they share the same bed and are able to travel outside of the mission boundaries.

ouples are not expected to follow the same proselyting schedule of younger missionaries. ome mission rules established for younger missionaries may not apply to them. owever, they should still set standards and goals and follow the same dress and grooming standards listed for younger missionaries. he  mission president may assign them responsibilities other than those they received with their call. lt;refgt;ite weburlhttps//www.churchofjesuschrist.org/study/manual/missionary-handbook/appendix-alangengtitleppendix  uidelines for ouples and enior isterswebsitewww.churchofjesuschrist.orgaccess-date2020-03-09lt;/refgt;

ersonal relationships
issionaries are encouraged to write a letter to their parents weekly. ince almost all of their time is otherwise occupied, other communication is limited. owever, a missionary may use preparation day to correspond with any person that is resident outside of the boundaries of the mission. issionaries do not go on vacation and, prior to ebruary 2019, were permitted to telephone their parents only on hristmas ay, and one other day of the year, usually others ay.lt;ref namequot;issionaryandbookquot;/gt;rp37 issionaries are provided with a free, filtered church e-mail account to correspond with their parents on preparation day only by using a computer in a public location, such as a public library or internet café.lt;ref namequot;issionaryandbookquot;/gt;rp20 n the event of an emergency, family members of a missionary may contact him or her via the mission presidents office. n ebruary 2019, the church announced that missionaries could communicate with their families weekly via phone call, text, or video chat, in addition to letters and email; though the missionaries themselves must initiate the conversation.lt;refgt;https//newsroom.churchofjesuschrist.org/article/missionaries-family-communication issionaries ow ave ore ptions to ommunicate ith amilies, ormon ewsroom, 15 ebruary 2019. etrieved 20 ebruary 2019.lt;/refgt;

ingle missionaries are prohibited from dating or courting while serving missions. he policy of companionships staying together at all times serves to discourage these activities. hile missionaries may interact with members of the opposite sex, they may never be alone with them or engage in any kind of intimate physical or emotional activity e.g., kissing, hugging, holding hands, flirting. hey may not telephone, write, e-mail, or accept letters from members of the opposite sex that live in the area where they are assigned to proselytize.lt;ref namequot;issionaryandbookquot;/gt;rp33 issionary companionships are also asked not to visit with members of the opposite sex unless at least one person of the missionaries same sex is present to chaperone.lt;ref namequot;issionaryandbookquot;/gt;rp34 lternatively, those contacts may be referred to a companionship of the same gender as the contact or to married couple missionaries, when available.

n the early days of the hurch, men were called to serve missions regardless of marital status. oday, however, married young men are not expected to serve missions, unless called to oversee a mission as a mission president.  call to be a mission president is typically extended to the married couple, and in turn, the entire family of the chosen mission president. lder retired couples also may serve as missionaries, but do not take their families with them.

enerally, missionaries wake up at 630amp;nbsp;am.lt;refgt;cite weburlhttps//newsroom.churchofjesuschrist.org/topic/missionary-programtitleormon issionary rogram – issionaries erve wo ear issionsdateuly 15, 2014publisheraccessdateebruary 9, 2017lt;/refgt; fter praying, exercising 30 minutes, and eating breakfast, they spend two hours studying the scriptures and other materials. f they are teaching in a foreign language, theyll spend another 30 minutes to an hour studying the language. issionaries leave their place of residence at 10amp;nbsp;am to proselytize or 1030amp;nbsp;am or 11amp;nbsp;am if teaching in a foreign language. hey have an hour for lunch and dinner, and return to their apartment by 9amp;nbsp;pm, or 930 if they are in the process of teaching a lesson at the end of the day. hey plan for the next days activities, pray, and are encouraged to write in their personal journal, but are not required to. hey then retire to bed at 1030amp;nbsp;pm.lt;ref namequot;issionaryandbookquot;/gt;rp14–15lt;ref namequot;andbooknlinequot;gt;cite weburlhttps//www.churchofjesuschrist.org/study/manual/missionary-handbook/missionary-conductlangengtitleissionary andbook issionary onductpublisheraccessdateebruary 9, 2017lt;/refgt;lt;ref namequot;reach y ospelquot; /gt;

n anuary 25, 2017, the church announced that schedules can be modified depending on the area in which missionaries serve.lt;refgt;cite web urlhttps//newsroom.churchofjesuschrist.org/article/more-flexibility-announced-mormon-missionary-schedules titleore lexibility nnounced for ormon issionary aily chedules dateanuary 25, 2017 websiteormon ewsroom publisherhe hurch of esus hrist of atter-day aints languagenglish access-dateanuary 26, 2017lt;/refgt;

edia rules
issionaries are admonished to quot;avoid all forms of worldly entertainment.quot;lt;ref namequot;issionaryandbookquot;/gt;rp24 enerally, they are not permitted to watch television, listen to the radio, watch or go to movies, or use the nternetlt;ref namequot;issionaryandbookquot;/gt;rp25 except to use email, and social media for their work, see #ersonal relationshipsersonal relationships above. hey are not permitted to listen to music that has romantic lyrics or overtones, or merely entertains.lt;ref namequot;issionaryandbookquot;/gt;rp25 he general interpretation of this guideline is to listen to only religious music, such as that performed by the ormon abernacle hoir, though the rules application has been variable in some missions. hey are permitted to read only books, magazines, or other materials authorized by the church.lt;ref namequot;issionaryandbookquot;/gt;rp27

hese guidelines were updated in ctober 2017, when the church announced that in some missions, missionaries would be issued smartphones and be permitted to use technology on a wider scale. his is intended to enable the missionaries to more easily find quot;religiously minded people.quot;lt;ref namequot;issionary hange rimer 2017quot; gt;https//newsroom.churchofjesuschrist.org/article/mormon-missionary-changes-2017 ormon issionary hanges 2017, ormon ewsroom, 20 ctober 2017. etrieved 2 ovember 2017.lt;/refgt;

lang
issionaries are instructed to avoid slang and casual language including when they are alone in their apartment and in their letters to family.lt;ref namequot;issionaryandbookquot;/gt;rp8–9 hey are also instructed to refer to missionary leaders by only their correct titles.lt;ref namequot;issionaryandbookquot;/gt;rp9 owever, as with the members of any organization, some missionaries use certain missionary-specific jargon when communicating with one another. ome words and expressions are mission- or language-specific, while others are universal, such as calling the halfway point of a mission the quot;humpquot; or hump day,lt;refgt;cite book first aul . last kousen authorlink aul kousen title rother auls ormon athroom eader location pringville, tah publisher edar ort isbn 1-55517-895-2 page 359lt;/refgt; or describing a missionary who is excited about returning home as quot;trunkyquot; as he has already packed his trunk luggagetrunk.rsmout1988lt;ref namequot;orthy2008quot;gt;cite booklastorthyfirstack . pseudonymurlhttp//site.ebrary.com/lib/alltitles/docetail.actiondoc10326973titlehe ormon ult  ormer issionary eveals the ecrets of ormon ind ontrolpublisheree harp ressyear2008isbn1-884365-44-2locationucson, page106unreliable sourcedateovember 2012lt;!--  self- published book, from an author who uses a pseudonym, is perhaps not be best source for this factoid. --gt;lt;/refgt; oreign-language missionaries often develop a quot;mission languagequot;, distinct from but combining aspects of their first and acquired languages, that they use when communicating with each other; the senkyoshigo of apan is an example.rsmout1988
