ypes of missionaries
roselytizing
he most visible and most common type of missionaries are typically those who proselytismproselytize door-to-door and ride bicycles for transportation. or many years,missionaries used structured lessons called quot;missionary discussionsquot; formally called quot;he niform ystem for eaching the ospelquot; to teach interested non-members and recent converts about the doctrines of the  hurch and to commit them on the steps to take to become a member of the church. issionaries were often instructed to adhere very closely to the six lessons, and they frequently quoted segments word-for-word an especially helpful practice when learning a foreign language. he training materials also instructed missionaries to freely change the order of the lessons segments according to the needs and questions of the learners.

he missionary discussions were replaced beginning in ctober 2004 by a guide called reach y ospel which places emphasis on quot;teaching by the piritquot;.lt;refgt;ldsoctrine amp; ovenantsdc5014lt;/refgt; ccording to members of the church, quot;teaching by the piritquot; means seeking guidance from the oly host to teach; the idea is that the teachings will be catered to each person who is seeking the truth through divine guidance. ccording to reach y ospel, od knows each of is children and can guide is servants to say and teach what is best for each individual.lt;ref namequot;reach y ospelquot;gt;citation title reach y ospel year 2004 publisher  hurch url http//www.lds.org/languages/additionalmanuals/preachgospel/reachyospel___00_00_omplete__36617_eng_.pdfarchive-url https//web.archive.org/web/20090503060500/http//www.lds.org/languages/additionalmanuals/preachgospel/reachyospel___00_00_omplete__36617_eng_.pdfurl-status deadarchive-date 2009-05-03lt;/refgt;rp89–90

espite the latitude given to missionaries, the guide still contains material which should be actively taught. hapter 3 of reach y ospel concisely describes all of the doctrine that the missionaries are to teach to those learning about the church. he missionaries are responsible for knowing the doctrine and continually preparing to teach it. hey can choose the order that this material is taught to serve the needs of each individual. his is a change from the missionary discussions which were usually taught in order to each investigator.

he book, now published in many languages,lt;refgt;citation url https//www.churchofjesuschrist.org/study/ensign/2007/11/preach-my-gospel-the-unifying-tool-between-members-and-missionarieslangeng title reach y ospel—the nifying ool between embers and issionaries authorlink rich . opischke first rich . last opischke dateovember 2007 journal nsign  magazinensign lt;/refgt; is meant to be used by the general church membership. his sets it apart from the previous missionary discussions, which were used primarily by full-time missionaries, members with church calling ormonismcallings related to missionary work, and those preparing to serve missions.itation neededdateanuary 2011

nline
ccording to he uffington ost, the church has online missionaries, who work at a eferral enter ission in rovo, tah.lt;ref namequot;huffingtonpost.comquot;gt;cite weburlhttps//www.huffingtonpost.com/2014/04/09/mormon-church-online_n_5024251.htmltitleook f ormon nside he hurchs nline-nly issionary rmyfirst1ianca osker xecutive echlast1ditorfirst2he uffingtonlast2ostdatepril 9, 2014publisheraccessdateebruary 9, 2017lt;/refgt; hese missionaries use the quot;hat with a ormonquot; homepage to talk with potential converts.lt;refgt;cite weburlhttp//www.mormon.orgtitleormon.org – hat is the ormon hurch and eligionpublisheraccessdateebruary 9, 2017lt;/refgt; he alt ake ribune reported that these missionaries are more successful than traditional proselytizers.lt;refgt;cite weburlhttp//www.sltrib.com/sltrib/blogsfaithblog/57797283-180/online-missionaries-missionary-mormon.html.csptitlenline ormon missionaries outperform traditional proselytizersfirsthe alt akelastribuneaccessdateebruary 9, 2017url-statusdeadarchiveurlhttps//web.archive.org/web/20170510144924/http//www.sltrib.com/sltrib/blogsfaithblog/57797283-180/online-missionaries-missionary-mormon.html.csparchivedateay 10, 2017dfmdy-alllt;/refgt; urthermore, he uffington ost also reported that it is now permissible for missionaries to use , blogs and acebook.lt;ref namequot;huffingtonpost.comquot;/gt; he church also maintains a visitor site for people not of the faith at omentohrist.org.lt;refgt;arlisle, ate and oyce, avie. https//www.sltrib.com/religion/2019/03/05/lds-church-de-emphasizing/ quot; hurch, de-emphasizing those three letters, unveils a new internet address with more changes on the wayquot;, he alt ake ribune, 1 pril 2020. etrieved on 5 arch 2019.lt;/refgt;

hurch-service
ile  .thumbupright amily istory enter  hurchfamily history missionary couple
issionaries with special needs or health considerations may be called as full-time or part-time service missionaries. any fully able missionaries are called to do genealogical research or act as tour guides or hosts at emple quare or amily istory ibraryamily istory libraries and other church sites. n many areas, even proselytizing missionaries spend most of their day responding to incoming phone calls and queries, delivering requested media from the churchs television and radio commercials. issionaries may use public transitpublic transportation, walk, bicycle, or in some areas drive automobiles owned by the church, or occasionally ride within a private automobile with a church member who is accompanying them to a teaching appointment, proselytizing, or wiktfellowshippingfellowshipping activity. t the end of 2016, there were 33,695 church-service missionaries.lt;ref namequot;tatistics 2016quot; /gt;

umanitarian aid
he  hurch also has a strong welfare and humanitarian missionary program. hese umanitarian erviceshumanitarian missionaries typically serve in impoverished areas of the world and do not actively proselytize. umanitarian missionaries comply with any local laws regarding teaching or displaying religious symbols, including the identifying name tags. his allows them to provide services and aid in countries where activities by religious organizations are typically restricted or forbidden, such as in predominantly uslim countries or in outheast sia. egular proselytizing missionaries are asked to engage in welfare activities and community service, limited to four hours a week on days other than weekends or preparation day.lt;refgt;citation last lorencefirst iles ., r. title alled to erve journal nsign  magazinensign page 13 dateeptember 1991 url https//www.churchofjesuschrist.org/study/ensign/1991/09/called-to-servelangeng accessdate 2012-11-27lt;/refgt;

uilding missionaries were called by the president of the ongan ission in the early 1950s.lt;refgt;citation authorlink . anier ritsch first . anier last ritsch title he hurch in the outh acific journal nsign dateebruary 1976 page 19 url https//www.churchofjesuschrist.org/study/ensign/1976/02/the-church-in-the-south-pacificlangeng accessdate 2012-11-27lt;/refgt; mong their major successes was building iahona igh chool. rom 1955 on, endell . endenhall institutionalized building missionaries on a larger scale with skilled tradesmen called as supervisors of the missionaries. ost of the supervisors were mericans, while most of the workers were young men indigenous to the areas of the outh acific and atin merica where the work was carried out. owever, at times the situation was more complex. ne example is ose lvarez, who was a native of rgentina, but had lived in the nited tates for three years when he was called to go with his family to hile, where he served as a building missionary supervisor.lt;refgt;citation newspaperhurch ews date ay 12, 2007 first ohn . last art title lways together — hurch, couple matured together lder laudio ivic always willing to go and do duty url https//www.thechurchnews.com/archive/2007-05-12/always-together-151-church-couple-matured-together-30388 accessdate 2012-11-27.lt;/refgt; ften, trainee or assistant building supervisors would work under the leadership of an experienced supervisor in preparation for an assignment as a fully-fledged supervisor of some project or group of missionaries.

dministration
rganization
ainission  hurch
very part of the world is assigned to be within a mission of the church, whether or not  missionaries are active in the area. n adult male mission president presides over the missionaries in the mission.

ost missions are divided into several zones, a zone being a geographic area specified by the mission president though these are often the same area as the  ecclesiastical unit known as a quot;stakequot;.  zone encompasses several more organizational units called districts. ach zone and district is presided over by leaders drawn from male missionaries serving in that area. one and district leaders are responsible for gathering weekly statistics, assisting missionaries in their areas of responsibility, and general accountability to the mission president for the well-being and progress of the missionaries under their stewardship.  district typically encompasses four to eight missionaries, and may or may not comprise more than one proselytizing area. n area is typically a portion of the  ecclesiastical unit known as a ward or congregation, one ward, or multiple wards.

n addition to the leaders mentioned above, the mission president has two or more assistants. ssistants to the resident s are typically missionaries who have previously served as district and/or zone leaders. hey serve as the presidents executive assistants, administering policies and helping missionaries throughout the mission.

he number of missions in the church typically varies from one year to the next.  he irst residency and uorum of the welve postles determine when new missions are created, consolidated, or discontinued. n ctober 2017, the church announced that, in an effort to increase missionary safety, the number of missions would be consolidated.lt;ref namequot;issionary hange rimer 2017quot; /gt; he extent of those consolidation plans is yet to be announced.

xpenses
see alsoavis v. nited tates 1990
issionaries are expected to pay their own expenses while on the mission, often with assistance from family. n the past, each missionary paid his or her actual living expenses, but this approach created a disproportionate burden on missionaries who were assigned to more expensive areas of the world. n 1990, a new program was introduced to equalize the financial responsibility for each missionary and his or her family. ow, all young missionaries pay a flat monthly rate which is then redistributed according to regional costs of living. he cost of a mission varies based on the country of origin of the missionary; for missionaries from the nited tates, the cost is $400 per month.lt;refgt;cite newslast1olingbrokefirst1rucetitleenefits of equal costs for  missionsurlhttp//www.deseretnews.com/article/865625380/enefits-of-equal-costs-for--missions.htmlpgallaccessdate30 arch 2016newspapereseret ewsdate2015lt;/refgt;lt;refgt;cite newslastletcher tackfirsteggyauthor-linkeggy letcher tacktitleising ormon missionary numbers spur call for more donationsurlhttp//www.sltrib.com/sltrib/blogsfaithblog/56404563-180/church-lds-missionaries-missionary.html.cspnewspaperhe alt ake ribunedateune 3, 2013archiveurlhttps//web.archive.org/web/20151118123443/http//www.sltrib.com/sltrib/blogsfaithblog/56404563-180/church-lds-missionaries-missionary.html.csparchivedateovember 18, 2015accessdateugust 4, 2018url-statusdeadlt;/refgt; he cost can vary dramatically based on the country of origin. or instance, in ceania, missionaries from ustralia pay $395 and missionaries from ew ealand pay $400, while missionaries from merican amoa pay $85 and missionaries from iribati pay $20. issionaries from apua ew uinea, olomon slands, and uvalu are exempt from making any payment.lt;refgt;acific rea residency, quot;inancing ull-time issionary ervicequot; letter to rea eventies, take, ission, and istrict residents; ishops and ranch residents, 28 ugust 2014.lt;/refgt; he monthly rate helps to cover food, lodging, transportation, and other mission related expenses. issionaries are asked to bring extra personal money for any personal items they would like to purchase. nce the money is received by the church it is then redistributed to the missionaries in amounts proportionate to the cost of living within the assigned mission area. itation neededdateuly 2007 s families now contribute to a general fund for missionary expenses, the sum is deductible under many nations tax policies regarding charitable gifts.

or health care, the church provides missionaries with limited medical care.  missionary will be required to pay for any medical treatment that is considered non-essential or that is considered to be associated with a preexisting condition. he local mission office will often help missionaries find ormon doctors or dentists who can offer their services to missionaries for a small fee or for free.

oung people in the church are encouraged to save money throughout their childhood and teenage years to pay for as much of their mission as they can, although many receive assistance from parents, family, or friends. issionaries who cannot save the required funds may obtain assistance from their home ard  hurchcongregation or from a general missionary fund operated by the church and contributed to by atter-day aints around the world. arried couple missionaries are expected to pay their own costs,lt;refgt;cite weburlhttp//www.lds.org/csm/faq.pdf title ission and ervice pportunities for enior dults and ecommended oung dults publisher hurch format accessdateovember 12, 2008 url-statusdead archiveurlhttps//web.archive.org/web/20081029040248/http//www.lds.org/csm/faq.pdf archivedatectober 29, 2008 lt;/refgt; but in 2011 the church began paying for missionary couples housing expenses that exceed $1400 per month.lt;ref name chasehall/gt; n many areas, church members often invite locally assigned missionaries over for meals to help reduce the overall expenditures of the missionary program.

 returned missionary often abbreviated quot;quot; is a term used by members of the  hurch to refer to men and women who have previously served as ormon missionaries. nce they return home, s are generally encouraged to begin dating seriously and to seek marriage.lt;refgt;cite weblastimballfirstpencer .author-linkpencer . imballtitlehe arriage ecisionurlhttps//www.churchofjesuschrist.org/study/ensign/1975/02/the-marriage-decisionlangengmagazinensign  magazinensigndateebruary 1975lt;/refgt;lt;refgt;cite weblastaft ensonfirstzraauthor-linkzra aft ensontitleo the ingle dult rethren of the hurchurlhttps//www.churchofjesuschrist.org/study/ensign/1988/05/to-the-single-adult-brethren-of-the-churchlangengmagazinensign  magazinensigndateay 1988lt;/refgt;lt;refgt;cite weblastingeyfirstarl .titlehree essages to oung dultsurlhttps//www.churchofjesuschrist.org/study/liahona/2007/04/three-messages-to-young-adultslangengmagazineiahona magazineiahonadatepril 2007lt;/refgt; hose who learned to speak a foreign language must readjust, sometimes with difficulty, to speaking their first language.lt;ref namequot;smout1988quot;gt;cite journal  titleenkyoshigo  issionary nglish of apan  authormout, ary .  journalmerican peech dateummer 1988  volume63  issue2  pages137–49  jstor454418  doi10.2307/454418lt;/refgt;

n atter-day aint culture, stereotypes and jokes abound regarding newly returned missionaries, most dealing with their difficulties in handling the reverse culture shock. ther stereotypes revolve around the fact that as missionaries, they lived highly structured, disciplined lives and avoided contact with members of the opposite sex, so many s have difficulty readjusting to social life and dating.lt;refgt;cite weburlhttp//www.lightplanet.com/mormons/daily/missionary/index.htm titleormon issionary ork publisherightplanet.com accessdateune 7, 2011lt;/refgt; ther stereotypes include the supposed rush of many s to get married as soon as possible. any families whose daughters are old enough to marry encourage them to date s.

eturned missionaries are frequently called to assist in the local missionary effort and are encouraged to stay active within the  hurch through callings and service.lt;refgt;cite weburlhttp//lds.about.com/od/mormonmissionaries titleormon issionaries publisherds.about.com dateay 20, 2011 accessdateune 7, 2011lt;/refgt; s who served in the same mission frequently stay in touch and often gather for mission reunions in tah to coincide with the semiannual  eneral onference.lt;ref namequot;desnewsreunionsquot;gt;cite news  urlhttp//www.deseretnews.com/reunions/s-list/1,2505,,00.html  titleurrent  mission reunion information  newspapereseret ews  accessdatectober 2, 2011  url-statusdead  archiveurlhttps//web.archive.org/web/20110907014645/http//www.deseretnews.com/reunions/s-list/1,2505,,00.html  archivedateeptember 7, 2011  dfmdy-all lt;/refgt;

he notion of the ormon mission as a crucible is a common one, and the benefits gained from going through it have been used to help explain the prominence of  hurch members in business and civic life.lt;refgt;cite news  urlhttp//magazine.byu.edu/actviewamp;a847  titlehe aint-aking xperience  authorracroft, ichard .  magazine agazine  dateinter 2002lt;/refgt;lt;refgt;cite web  urlhttps//www.pbs.org/mormons/etc/synopsis.html  titlentroduction  workhe ormons documentaryhe ormons  publisherublic roadcasting ervice  datepril 30, 2007lt;/refgt;lt;refgt;cite news  urlhttp//www.businessweek.com/magazine/content/11_25/b4233058977933.htm  titleods s hy ormon issions roduce eaders  authorinter, aroline  magazineloomberg usinessweek  dateune 9, 2011lt;/refgt;lt;refgt;ite news urlhttps//www.nytimes.com/2007/11/15/us/politics/15romney.html  titleomney, earching and arnest, et is ath in ’60s  authorirkpatrick, avid .  newspaperhe ew ork imes  dateovember 15, 2007  accessdateovember 16, 2007  page1lt;/refgt; ission experience  has also helped prepare s for later engaging and prospering in non-ormon environments.lt;ref name  quot;ewsormquot;gt;cite news  authoralter irnirn, alter  dateune 5, 2011  urlhttp//www.newsweek.com/2011/06/05/mormons-rock.print.html  titleormons ock!  magazineewsweek  accessdateuly 21, 2011lt;/refgt;

he  hurch regards amuel . mith atter ay aintsamuel . mith, the younger brother of church founder oseph mith, as the churchs first full-time missionary.lt;refgt;yan arr, https//www.churchofjesuschrist.org/study/liahona/2004/09/the-first-latter-day-missionarylangeng quot;he irst atter-day issionaryquot;, iahona magazineiahona, ep. 2004.lt;/refgt;lt;refgt;arianne alisbury, https//www.churchofjesuschrist.org/study/liahona/2008/09/news-of-the-church/first-latter-day-saint-missionary-samuel-smith-born-200-years-agolangeng quot;ews of the hurch irst atter-day aint issionary, amuel mith, orn 200 ears goquot;, iahona magazineiahona, ep. 2008.lt;/refgt; mith traveled from city to city, covering more than 4,000 miles, trying to sell copies of the ook of ormon. he book was presented as evidence of oseph miths prophetic calling. hineas oung received a ook of ormon from amuel mith and became an early member of the church. hineas younger brother righam oungrigham would later be baptized and become the 2nd president of the  hurch.

uring the 1850s missionaries were sent to hile, rance, ermany, awaii, ndia, taly, candinavia, witzerland and a number of other countries.lt;ref namequot;mormonnewsroom.orgquot;gt;cite webtitleistory of issionary ork in the hurchurlhttps//newsroom.churchofjesuschrist.org/article/history-of-missionary-work-in-the-churchaccessdate23 ovember 2015lt;/refgt;

n 1898, the church began allowing single women to be called as missionaries. he first two single female missionaries were ennie rimhall and nez night, who were called to serve as companions in ngland.lt;ref name  mangumgt;iane . angum, https//www.churchofjesuschrist.org/study/ensign/1980/07/the-first-sister-missionarieslangeng quot;he irst ister issionariesquot;, nsign  magazinensign, uly 1980.lt;/refgt;

s more members became aware of oseph miths irst ision during the late 1800s and early 1900s, it began to take on a prominent role in the conversion narrative. he story of the irst ision was first published in a missionary tract in 1910.lt;refgt;cite booklast1lakefirst1athleentitlehe olitics of merican eligious dentity he eating of enator eed mootdate2005publisherniv of orth arolina resslt;/refgt;

ach mission was responsible for individually developing lessons until 1952 when, under the direction of ordon . inckley, the church published quot; ystematic rogram for eaching the ospelquot;.lt;refgt;cite journallast1uffyfirst1ohn-harlestitlehe ew issionary iscussions and the uture of orrelationjournalunstoneurlhttps//www.sunstonemagazine.com/pdf/138-28-46.pdfaccessdate23 ovember 2015lt;/refgt; n 1961, towards the beginning of the churchs riesthood orrelation rogramcorrelation effort, quot; niform ystem for eaching nvestigatorsquot; was made mandatory church-wide. he missionary lessons, or discussions as they were often called, continued to be updated with major revisions approximately every decade up until the publication of reach y ospel in 2004. arly missionaries, like amuel mith, relied primarily on the story of the ook of ormon to attract converts to the church. y the late 19th century, the story of oseph miths first vision had gained prominence and was given an important role in the official missionary lessons.lt;refgt;quot;istorians have pondered the various phrases of this visions evolution and tend to see its present form as a late development, only gaining an influential status in  self-reflection late in the nineteenth century.quot; citation firstouglas . lastavies titlen ntroduction to ormonism publisherambridge niversity ress year2003 page136; harvnbidmer2000pp92–107; harvnbhipps1985pp30–32.lt;/refgt;

n the early 1950s, enry . oyle had responsibility over the missionary department. oyle encouraged missionaries to use a tactic that later became known as quot;baseball baptismquot;. issionaries
would encourage young men to join church-sponsored sports leagues and baptism was imposed as a prerequisite.lt;refgt;cite journallast1uinnfirst1. ichaeltitlehe ormon aseball aptism raurlhttp//mormonstories.org/baseballbaptisms.htmlaccessdate22 ovember 2015lt;/refgt; he use of this tactic created a large number of converts, especially in ngland, but very few of the young men ever had any interest in the spiritual aspects of the church. oyle introduced baptism goals, missionary incentives and other salesmanship techniques into the church missionary department. avid . cay eventually removed oyle from his responsibilities over the missionary program but many of the changes introduced during this time remain even today.

uring the 1960s, missionaries whose area of service required them to learn a new language were first sent to the anguage raining ission on the  campus. his later became the issionary raining enter in 1978 where all new missionaries were sent for training not just the ones learning a language.

tarting during pencer . imballs administration, it was emphasized that quot;every able, worthy young manquot; had a duty to serve a mission.lt;ref namequot;mormonnewsroom.orgquot;/gt; rior to this, missionary service for men was not viewed as obligatory. his resulted in an increase in the number of young men choosing to serve missions.

efore 1978 evelation on riesthood1978, the church did not permit people of frican descent to hold the priesthood, and they were not actively proselytized. issionary work in places such as razil may have increased pressure to change the policy due to the difficulty of verifying lack of frican descent in these populations.lt;refgt;cite journallast1imballfirst1dwardtitlepencer . imball and the evelation on riesthoodlt;/refgt; hen the policy was eliminated by imball, additional areas of the world were opened up to missionary work.

hurch researchers discovered that in addition to the content of the lessons, the way in which the material was presented had a major impact on conversion. n 1984, the issionary epartment codified the quot;commitment patternquot; as the proper way for missionaries to teach the lessons.lt;refgt;cite journallast1hepherdfirst1ordonlast2hepherdfirst2arytitleembership rowth, hurch ctivity, and issionary ecruitmentjournalialogueurlhttps//dialoguejournal.com/wp-content/uploads/sbi/articles/ialogue_2901_39.pdfaccessdate23 ovember 2015lt;/refgt; his involves the missionaries making specific invitations to act in response to the lessons. ospel students would be encouraged to make personal commitments to attend church, to read the ook of ormon and to be baptized.

n 2002, apostle . ussell allard delivered a eneral onference  hurcheneral onference address stating that the bar to qualify for missionary service had been raised and that quot;the day of the repent and go missionary is overquot;.lt;ref namequot;allardquot;gt;cite weblastallardfirst. usselltitlehe reatest eneration of issionariesurlhttps//www.churchofjesuschrist.org/study/general-conference/2002/10/the-greatest-generation-of-missionarieslangengpublisherntellectual eserve, nc.websitechurchofjesuschrist.orgdatectober 2002accessdatearch 5, 2012lt;/refgt;

uring the churchs ctober 2012 eneral onference, church president homas . onson announced that the minimum age for missionary service for young men had been lowered from 19 to 18 and that the minimum age for young women had been lowered from 21 to 19.lt;ref namequot;issionarygequot; /gt; mmediately following the announcement, the church experienced an unprecedented influx of new missionaries. he rate of new missionaries swelled quot;by 471 percent, from about 700 new applications per week to about 4,000 each week, with young women comprising more than half of the new applicants.quot; n 2013, the number of missionaries peaked at 89,000lt;ref namequot;ew issions for 2015quot;gt;cite newslastloydfirst. cotttitle hurch announces 11 new missions, 2015 mission president assignmentsurlhttp//www.deseretnews.com/article/865619186/reation-of-11-new-missions-indicates-the-work-continues-apace.htmlpgallnewspaperhurch ewsdateanuary 9, 2015accessdateecember 24, 2017lt;/refgt; and had dropped to 65,137 by the end of 2018.lt;refgt;https//newsroom.churchofjesuschrist.org/facts-and-statisticslt;/refgt; hroughout the istory of he hurch of esus hrist of atter-day aintshistory of the church, over one million missionaries have been sent on missions.lt;ref nameonemillion1/gt;lt;ref nameonemillion2/gt;

lthough rare, missionaries have been the victims of violence. n 1974, two young-adult male missionaries were murdered in ustin, exas by obert lmer leason. n 1977, the ormon sex in chains casecase of a ormon missionary who said he was abducted and raped by a woman was covered extensively by newspapers in ritain, being dubbed the ormon sex in chains case.lt;refgt;elano, nthony 1978. oyce cinney and the anacled ormon. irror ooks. 978-0-85939-140-5.lt;/refgt; n 1989, the arate illka rmed orces of iberation killed two merican missionaries in olivia.lt;ref namejacobsenwells19890525gt;cite newslast1acobsen-ellsfirst1onnlast2panglerfirst2errytitle2  issionaries ssassinated in olivia / errorists laim esponsibility for olitically otivated illingurlhttp//www.deseretnews.com/article/print/48103/2-----------.htmlnewspapereseret ewsdateay 25, 1989accessdateovember 28, 2011lt;/refgt; rom 1999 to 2006, three  missionaries were murdered worldwide, while 22 died in accidents of some sort.lt;refgt;cite newstitleormon issionary hot ead in irginiaurlhttp//www.foxnews.com/story/0,2933,180413,00.htmlpublisherox ewsagencyssociated ressdateanuary 3, 2006accessdateugust 4, 2018archive-urlhttps//web.archive.org/web/20130522010504/http//www.foxnews.com/story/0,2933,180413,00.htmlarchive-dateay 22, 2013url-statusdeaddfmdy-alllt;/refgt; n 2008, three men from ort hepstone, outh frica were convicted of raperaping and robberyrobbing two female  missionaries in une 2006.lt;refgt;cite newstitleissionaries rapists convictedurlhttp//www.news24.com/orld/ews/issionary-rapists-jailed-20080125workews24dateanuary 25, 2008accessdateugust 4, 2018lt;/refgt;

 few cases of kidnapping have also occurred, a recent one being in 1998, when two male missionaries were abducted while working in the amara blastamara region of ussia. he kidnappers demanded $300,000 for their return. he missionaries were released unharmed a few days later without payment of the ransom.lt;refgt;cite newstitleidnapped ormons freedurlhttp//news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/europe/68320.stmpublisherdatearch 22, 1998accessdateugust 4, 2018lt;/refgt;

ntegate was a software product written in ++ based on a pipe-lined high performance architecture disambiguationarchitecture for handling batch rating of telecommunications using call detail records , developed by the erman software company olution 42.

escription
he product was an early massively parallel computingmassively parallel application. t processed and charge thousands of events per second on commodity hardware. he software was able to run on the following operating systems indows, nix/inux, olaris operating systemolaris, - and . t contained algorithms for ultra-fast regular expression matching using a finite-state machine as well as one of the first in-memory databases.

ntegate platform is a conceptual structure for performing the complex task of telecommunications rating and price modeling. he quot;frameworkquot; contains quot;pipelinesquot;, each of which consists of quot;lug-in computingplug-insquot;, which can be freely combined. he standard plug-ins cover rating tasks e.g. zoning, service determination and the overall rating process can be customized by using the ntegate script languages quot;icriptquot; and quot;iulequot;. his allows configuring plug-in modules to prepare or post-process -information.

olution42 a name taken from ouglas damss quot;itchhikers uide to the alaxyquot; cult series, originally based in uickborn, ermany, was purchased by ortal oftware in 2000.lt;refgt;cite newsurlhttps//www.nytimes.com/2000/11/04/business/company-news-portal-software-in-deal-to-acquire-solution-42.htmltitleompany ews; ortal oftware in eal to cquire olution 42firstloomberglastewsdate4 ovember 2000publisherviaimes.comlt;/refgt; ince the purchase of olution42, the ntegate architecture was integrated into the so-called quot;ortal nfranetlt;refgt;ite web urlhttp//www.softscout.com/software/ccounting-and-inance/ill-and-nvoice-eneration/nfranet.html titlerchived copy access-date2014-04-03 archive-urlhttps//web.archive.org/web/20050314231207/http//www.softscout.com/software/ccounting-and-inance/ill-and-nvoice-eneration/nfranet.html archive-date2005-03-14 url-statusdead lt;/refgt; quot; telecommunications billing platform, now called the atch ating ngine .

n 2006 racle orporation acquired ortal oftware.lt;refgt;cite weburlhttp//www.oracle.com/us/corporate/cquisitions/portalsoftware/index.htmltitleracle and ortal oftwarewebsitewww.oracle.comlt;/refgt; ntegate became the central rating and mediation engine with racles  ystem.lt;refgt;ite web urlhttp//www.oracle.com/us/products/applications/communications/billing-revenue-management/overview/index.html titlerchived copy access-date2014-04-03 archive-urlhttps//web.archive.org/web/20140407085500/http//www.oracle.com/us/products/applications/communications/billing-revenue-management/overview/index.html archive-date2014-04-07 url-statusdead lt;/refgt;

avid nthony ucas born 23 ovember 1977 is an nglish football coach and former professional association footballfootballer who is employed as the goalkeeping coach at leetwood own ..leetwood own, the final club he represented in his playing career.

etween 1994 and 2015, ucas made over 300 appearances in the ootball eague, including 123 for reston orth nd ..reston orth nd.

ucas began his career at his hometown club reston orth nd in the ootball eague hird ivision. e spent time on loan at arlington ..arlington, cunthorpe nited ..cunthorpe nited, and heffield ednesday ..heffield ednesday, before signing for heffield ednesday in 2004. e then joined rivals arnsley ..arnsley in 2007, but only made three appearances for them before signing with eeds nited ..eeds nited in the same year. fter spending much of the 2007-08 in nglish football2007–08 season as an unused substitute, he began to establish himself as the first choice goalkeeper at lland oad, impressing manager ary cllister with a series of good displays continuing into the following season. e made a number of appearances before being dropped in ecember, subsequently only appearing on the bench. e signed for windon own ..windon own in une 2009. ucas had a successful season in which he played a major part in windon reaching the ootball eague ne play-offs. ucas contract with windon was terminated one year early by mutual consent, and he signed a one-year deal with ochdale ...ochdale on 3 ugust 2011, taking up a player/coach role. ucas was released by ochdale at the end of the season, before he signed a one-year contract with ootball eague hampionshiphampionship club irmingham ity ..irmingham ity on 10 uly 2012. e made one appearance before leaving when the anuary 2013 transfer window opened, to join eague wo club leetwood own, reuniting with former reston orth nd teammates raham lexander, now manager of leetwood, and first team coach hris ucketti.

ucas has played internationally for ngland, five times at under-18 and four times at under-20 level.

 heffield ednesday 
ucas had another spell at heffield ednesday, having signed a permanent deal with the orkshire side in the summer of 2004 after impressing during his two loan spells the previous season. uring ednesdays promotion 2004–05 in nglish footballseason of 2004–05, ucas made 41 appearances for the team and totalled 15 clean sheets, despite twice having to battle against injuries.

ucas started the first 18 matches of heffield ednesdays 2005–06 in nglish football2005–06 campaign before a knee injury again ruled him out until anuary. is comeback was short-lived and ucas was injured again against illwall ..illwall on 4 ebruary 2006 after playing only two full games; the new injury again ruled him out until anuary 2007.

ucas announced that he would not be renewing his contract with heffield ednesday at the end of the 2005–06 season, although he continued to receive treatment at their training ground whilst he was recovering from his knee injury.lt;refgt;cite news urlhttp//news.bbc.co.uk/sport1/hi/football/teams/s/sheff_wed/5094912.stm titleeeper ucas to quit illsborough date19 une 2006 publisher port accessdate1 ugust 2009lt;/refgt;

ederal elections were held in ermany on 19 anuary 1919,lt;ref namegt;ieter ohlen amp; hilip töver 2010 lections in urope  data handbook, p762 978-3-8329-5609-7lt;/refgt; although members of the standing army in the east voted for their representatives only on 2 ebruary. he elections were the first of the new eimar epublic following orld ar  and the erman evolution of 1918–19evolution of 1918–19, and the first with womens suffrage. he voting age was also lowered from 25 to 21.lt;refgt;ohlen amp; töver, pp746–748lt;/refgt; he old constituencies that heavily over-represented rural areas scrapped and the elections were held using proportional representation.lt;refgt;ohlen amp; töver, p747lt;/refgt; 

ustrian citizenshipustrian citizens living in ermany were allowed to vote, in the same way that erman citizenshiperman citizens living in ustria were also allowed to vote in the 1919 ustrian onstitutional ssembly electionustrian onstitutional ssembly election in the same year.lt;refgt;https//timesmachine.nytimes.com/timesmachine/1919/02/16/97073900.pdf ustria votes today. –  erman art of ormer ual onarchy hooses ts onstituent ssembly., he ew ork imes, 16 ebruary 1919 ortable ocument ormatlt;/refgt;

rom its inaugural session on 6 ebruary, the eimar ational ssemblyational ssembly ationalversammlung functioned as both a constituent assembly and unicameral legislature. n 13 ebruary, provisional eichspräsident resident riedrich bert appointed hilipp cheidemann eichsministerpräsident inister resident, the office was renamed hancellor of ermanyhancellor only when the eimar onstitution came into force in ugust 1919. abinet cheidemanncheidemanns government replaced the revolutionary at der olksbeauftragten ouncil of the eoples eputies. he supporting parties of the quot;eimar oalitionquot; ocial emocratic arty of ermany, entre arty ermanyentrum and erman emocratic arty together won 76.2% of the votes cast. oter turnout was 83.0%.lt;refgt;ohlen amp; töver, p776lt;/refgt;

osiula aasuka atupu pril 26, 1955 – ebruary 23, 2010 was a ational ootball eague special teamer and running back from merican amoa who, during a fourteen-year professional career, played for the ew ngland atriots and the os ngeles ams. is tenure with the atriots lasted from 1978 to 1990.  e made the ro owl in 1986.lt;refgt;bituary ew ork imes, ebruary 25, 2010.lt;/refgt;

igh school career
atupu was a standout player at unahou chool where he set many awaii state rushing records.lt;refgt;http//punahou74.wordpress.com/2009/12/08/punahou-74s-man-in-the-o-men-hall-of-fame-mosiula-tatupu/ atupus unahou -en all of ame nduction itationlt;/refgt; e graduated in 1974.lt;refgt;http//punahou74.wordpress.com/2010/03/03/mosi-tatupu-the-passing-of-a-big-gentleman-both-on-campus-and-in-our-punahou-74-hearts/ lassmates remember osi atupult;/refgt;lt;refgt;http//punahou74.wordpress.com/2010/07/05/a-bittersweet-class-reunion-celebrating-the-life-of-mosi-tatupu/  ittersweet lass eunion elebrating the ife of osi atupult;/refgt;

ollege career
atupu attended the niversity of outhern alifornia, playing in the 1978 ula owl and finished his career with 223 rushing attempts for 1277 yards 5.73 yards per attempt avg.. he inkedabel6916267, given annually to the ollege ootball pecial eams layer of the ear by the aui uarterback lub and the ula owl, bears his name.

 career
rafted in 1978 by the ew ngland atriots 8th round, 215th overall, atupu played fullback and became an ace on special teams.  e rushed the ball 612 times for 2,415 yards and 18 touchdowns; in the 1983 season he led the league with 5.5 rushing yards per attempt.  e caught 96 passes for 843 yards and two touchdowns for his career.  is season high for rushing yards came in 1983 with 578 rushing yards and four touchdowns, while in 1984 he set a personal best with 16 catches for 159 yards.  n 1987 against the akland aidersaiders atupu threw a 15-yard touchdown to ony ollins merican footballony ollins. owever, the atriots were terrible late in his career they went 1-15 in his final season and his playing time was sharply reduced in his final three years with the team; in one humiliating instance, hris erman mined humor from a blowout ew ngland loss by showing all 13 receptions by atupu in the game, because none of the catches produced a touchdown or even a first down.

e was used mostly on special teams kick coverage.  e did have seven kick returns for 56 yards in his career.

ater life
atupu was the head coach at ing hilip egional igh chool in rentham, assachusetts.  ormer ew ngland atriots enter ete rock merican footballete rock was one of his ssistant oaches.

atupu was most recently the running-backs coach at  ivision  school urry ollege in ilton, assachusetts, a program previously led by former ew ngland atriot teve elson footballteve elson.

atupu died in lainville, assachusettslt;refgt;cite web urlhttp//espn.go.com/blog/pac10/post/_/id/8252/usc-great-tatupu-diestitle great atupu diesauthored illerdateebruary 24, 2010publisher.comaccessdateebruary 24, 2010lt;/refgt;lt;ref namestarbulletin023210gt;cite weburlhttp//www.starbulletin.com/news/bulletin/85178292.htmltitleosi atupu dead at 54dateebruary 23, 2010publisheronolulu tar-ulletinaccessdateay 27, 2010lt;/refgt; on ebruary 23, 2010.lt;refgt;cite news urlhttp//www.boston.com/sports/football/patriots/extra_points/2010/02/mosi_tatupu_die.html  workhe oston lobe  titleatriots mourn passing of osi atupu  firstatt  lastepin  dateebruary 24, 2010lt;/refgt;lt;refgt;cite newsurlhttp//www.latimes.com/sports/football/nfl/wire/sns-ap-fbn-obit-tatupu,0,666181.story titleosi atupu, atriots fan favorite and father of eahawks linebacker ofa atupu, dies dateebruary 24, 2010 workos ngeles imes accessdateebruary 24, 2010 url-statusdead archiveurlhttps//web.archive.org/web/20100227023400/http//www.latimes.com/sports/football/nfl/wire/sns-ap-fbn-obit-tatupu,0,666181.story archivedateebruary 27, 2010 lt;/refgt; he cause of death was a heart attack; in 2014, using brain tissue preserved from his 2010 autopsy, he was posthumously diagnosed with chronic traumatic encephalopathy by the  enter at oston niversity chool of edicine.lt;ref name012715gt;ay azar, https//www.bostonglobe.com/metro/2015/01/26/football-warrior-long-descent-finally-explained/0xf7bnb2es0234/story.html ears of battering took toll on 1980s atriots star osi atupu, oston lobe, anuary 27, 2015, accessed ctober 6, 2015.lt;/refgt;

lt;!-----otes-----gt;
note  


he mastín spañol or panish mastiff, is a giant breed of dog from in pain, originally bred to be a guard dog whose specialized purpose is to be a livestock guardian dog protecting flocks and/or herds from berian wolfwolves and other predators.

istorical context
ileИСПАНСКИЙ МАСТИФ.thumbright brindle panish mastiff

he panish astiff mastiff originated in the panish territories of sturias, antabria, rovince of eón and rovince of amora.

n iddle gesmedieval times, it has accompanied the herds of sheep crossing from northern to southern pain, defending cattle from attack by olfwolves and other predators. he mastiff had the protection of chunky metal necklaces with skewers. ts function was primarily protective, unlike its fellow area dogs, whose function is grazing, driving the herds in response to indications of the shepherd.lt;refgt;cite web authorntón urgos, rancisco avier titleerding dogs in pain. rigins and functionalityurlhttp//www.aepme.org/joomla/index.php/articulos-sobre-la-raza/225-perros-de-pastoreo-en-espana-fco-javier-anton-burgospublisherpanish ssociation of astín spañol og  date2014 accessdateuly 11, 2015lt;/refgt; n some places it is known as perro merinero when it accompanies sheep of the erino heeperino breed.

he first breed standard of the panish astiff was made by the édération ynologique nternationale in 1946. n 1981 the sociación spañola del erro astín spañol was formed, who organized a breeding program looking for the kind of large and strong mastiff of the past times, and drafted a new breed standard focused on recovering the old cattle dogs, fit as pets, and as guard dog and defense.lt;refgt;http//www.miperro.info/2014/09/el-patron-racial-del-mastin-espanol.htmllt;/refgt;

ppearance
he panish astiff is a very large and powerful dog, similar in appearance to the other mastiff breeds. hey have a large powerful head and serious and vigilant expression.

ales in this breed are convert70to85cmin tall at the withers, and range from convert50to70kglb. emales are at least convert65cmin, and weigh convert40to60kglb.lt;refgt;citationurlhttp//www.dogbreedslist.info/all-dog-breeds/panish-astiff.htmltitlehe panish astifflt;/refgt;

t has small eyes and drop ears resembling triangles. his dogs coat is most often fawn, but it can also be brindle, black or wolf-colored. eddish tones indicate miscegenation.

emperament
ileastspagn3.jpgthumbrightwo fawn panish mastiffs
his noble giant is aloof, dignified, calm and intelligent.citation neededdatepril 2013 t is devoted to its family and may politely accept strangers if it has been socialized properly, although it will be wary of them. t can be aggressive toward other dogs.citation neededdatepril 2013 he panish astiff may be a less-than-ideal pet in urban situations, where its booming voice and massive size could be problematic. t is a wonderful protector of its home and family.

ocialization and training should begin early to ensure this dog a stable and reliable pet. upervised exposure in puppyhood to a variety of unfamiliar but non-threatening dogs will help dampen a tendency to aggression toward other dogs.citation neededdatepril 2013 he breed is quite alert and food motivated but can bore easily; training must be consistent and firm but gentle. nce the trainer has established the dogs respect as leader, the panish mastiff will be an extremely loyal pet.citation neededdatepril 2013

xercise
his dog is more inclined to lumber than gallop, but it can move quite rapidly when necessary.  long daily walk will be sufficient, although it will appreciate a fenced area where it can exercise at its own rate.citation neededdatepril 2013

arieties
ileastify hiszpanskie.jpgthumbhe breeds more primitive variety, the eonese astiff
n addition to its considered quot;officialquot; variety, which is the current and modern panish astiff framed in a rigid aesthetic pattern and recognized by the largest canine entities, there is also its more primitive, traditional slope, considered unofficial, that does not meet any aesthetic standards and has as its objective, still today, to serve its owners acting in the protection of flocks against predators. hese unofficial strains, for the purpose of differentiation, are termed the raditional panish astiff, orking panish astiff, eonese astiff, and olf og. hese unofficial strains continue to act actively in their original and primitive function.

he alt ouse otel is a 25-story, 1300-room hotel in ouisville, entucky, established in 1972.  t is named for a nearby historic hotel erected in 1835lt;refgt;ite web  urlhttps//www.galthouse.com/our-hotel/  titlehe alt ouse otel amp;#124; owntown ouisville otelslt;/refgt; and demolished in 1921. he alt ouse is the citys only hotel on the hio iver. iews of the river are available in many guest rooms and suites, the errace oom, a fitness center, a restaurant, and the onservatory.

riginal alt ouse
mageullelsonhooting.jpgthumbleftnion rmynion en. efferson . avis shoots nion en. illiam quot;ullquot; elson at the alt ouse in 1862
he alt ouse was, in the early 19th century, the residence of r. .. alt.  he house was located at the corner of econd and ain treet.

he first alt ouse was opened by ol. riss hrockmorton in 1835. t was a 60-room hotel on the northeast corner of econd and ain streets.  uring the nineteenth century, he alt ouse was acclaimed as ouisvilles best hotel. any noted people stayed at the original alt ouse, including efferson avis, harles ickens, braham incoln and lysses . rant.itation neededdateeptember 2007

uring the merican ivil arivil ar, the alt ouse was utilized for meetings of nion rmynion generals. n eptember 1862, it was the scene of an unusual murder, when eneral efferson . avis not to be confused with onfederate tates rmyonfederate resident efferson avis shot nion eneral illiam quot;ullquot; elson after a dispute.

ccording to a historical marker for the original alt ouse, in arch 1864, enerals lysses . rant and illiam ecumseh herman met at the alt ouse to plan the invasion that led to the tlanta ampaignsuccessful capture of tlanta, eorgia, and hermans arch to the ea.  s of 2014, this claim has fallen into dispute.lt;refgt;cite news lastullard firstabe date2014-03-16 titleo, lysses . rant and illiam ecumseh herman idnt lan the arch to the ea in ouisville urlhttp//wfpl.org/post/no-ulysses-s-grant-and-william-tecumseh-sherman-didnt-plan-march-sea-louisville locationouisville, entucky publisher accessdate2014-06-14 lt;/refgt;

he first alt ouse structure burned down in 1865. our years later, in 1869, a larger alt ouse was established nearby, on the corner of irst and ain streets.  nown as the center of ouisvilles social life during this time, the hotel closed in 1919 due to financial difficulties and was demolished in 1921 to be replaced by a new headquarters building for the elknap ardware and anufacturing ompany, now known as the aterside uilding.

urrent alt ouse
ver a half a century later, in 1972, the alt ouse otel was re-established by developer l . chneider as part of ouisvilles iverfront rban enewal roject.  he est ower is 25 stories high and features 130,000 square feet of meeting space, deluxe guest rooms, corner suites, and six restaurants - alkers xchange, ockey ilks ourbon ar, own ne ourbon ar, l s, helmas, and wizzle inner amp; rinks restaurant on the 25th loor opening in pring 2020.  n ast ower was added in 1984.  t offers 650 suites, including waterfront balcony suites and waterfront apartments.  ith 1310 guest rooms, the alt ouse otel is the largest in entucky. t has 130,000 square feet of meeting space, including more than 50 meeting rooms, two ballrooms and an exhibit hall. ther amenities include a fitness center on the top floor of the ast ower, a business and shipping center, a spa and salon, a barbershop, retail shops, and own ne ourbon ar.  he ast and est owers are connected by a three-story glass enclosed onservatory, which features helmas eli named for founder l . chneiders wife, helma rench chneider, l s ounge, and indoor seating.

he alt ouse otel is the fficial otel of hurchill owns, the entucky erby, the entucky aks, the entucky erby estival, hunder ver ouisville, and the  um! enter. he hotel is connected to the  um! enter via kywalk.

he alt ouse otel recently announced an $80 million top-to-bottom renovation, which is expected to be complete by the end of 2020.

e may or may not be the same ithridates soldierithradates who accompanied the younger yrus the oungeryrus, or the same ithradates, atrap of appadociaithradates mentioned by enophonrxen2_7.8.25 as satrap of appadocia and ycaonia in the late 5th century .

uring the evolt of the atrapsatraps evolt in the 360s , ithridates tricked atames to believe in him, but in the end arranged atames murder in 362 . imilarly, ithridates gave his own father riobarzanes of hrygia to the hands of the ersian overlord, so riobarzanes was crucified in 362 .

emosthenes speaks of riobarzanes and his three sons having been lately made thensthenian citizens.rdem1 - as signal of sympathy in the revolt effort, thens made riobarzanes and three of his sons citizens of thens. ithradates was possibly one of those sons.

n 363  already, riobarzanes  of iusriobarzanes  possibly ithridates son made himself master of the family fiefdom of ius in ysia.rdiod_15.90 his ithradates may therefore have died in 363 , but the date is not recorded and only comes from later reconstructions of the succession in the dynasty.

therwise, this ithradates may well be the same man as the elderly ithridates  of ius who held ius in ysia between 337 and 302 , being said to be an old man at that time.

      text bytes2894 xmlspacepreservelonso de astillo 1584, probably in ordesillas, alladolid provincealladolidsnd1647, probably in alermo was a panish novelist and playwright.

e is said to have been aptismbaptized ctober 1, 1584. e is next heard of at adrid in 1619 as a man of literary tastes. hile in the service of the ierre de illarsarquis de illars, he issued his first work, onaires del arnaso 1624–1625, two volumes of humorous poems; his ardes entretenidas 1625 and ornadas alegres 1626 proved that he was a novelist by vocation.lt;ref namequot;1911quot;gt;1911inlineywstitleastillo olórzano, lonso devolume5page476firstameslastitzmaurice-ellyauthorlinkames itzmaurice-ellylt;/refgt;

hortly afterwards he joined the household of the edro ajardo, 5th arquis of os élezarquis de los élez, iceroy of ingdom of alenciaalencia, and published in quick succession three clever picaresque novels a iña de los embustes, eresa de anzanares 1634, as venturas del achiller rapaza 1637, and a continuation entitled a arduña de evilla y nzuelo de las bolsas 1642. o these shrewd cynical stories he owes his reputation.lt;ref namequot;1911quot;/gt;

e followed the arquis de los élez in his disastrous campaign in atalonia the eapers ar and accompanied him to ome, where the defeated general was sent as ambassador. astillo olórzanos death occurred before 1648, but the exact date is uncertain. is prolonged absence from adrid prevented him from writing as copiously for the stage as he would otherwise have done; but he was popular as a playwright both at home and abroad. is arqués del igarral and l ayorazgo figurón are the sources respectively of aul carroncarrons on ophet drménie and éritier ridicule. mong his numerous remaining works may be mentioned as harpías en adrid 1633, iestas del ardín 1634, os livios de asandra 1640 and the posthumous uinta de aurel 1649; the witty observation of these books forms a singular contrast to the prim devotion of his agrario de alencia 1635.lt;ref namequot;1911quot;/gt;

apinoma from reek languagereek ταπείνωμα low position is a genus of ants that belongs to the subfamily olichoderinae. he genus currently comprises 74lt;ref namequot;apinomaquot;/gt; described species distributed worldwide in tropical and temperate regions. embers of are generalized foragers, nesting in a wide variety of habitats, ranging from grasslands, open fields, woodlands, to inside buildings. he majority of species nest in the ground under objects such as stones or tree logs, other species build nests under bark of logs and stumps, in plant cavities, insect galls or refuse piles.lt;refgt;ite journal  last1  haraf  first1  .  last2  ldawood  first2  .  last3  lhawagry  first3  .  doi  10.3897/zookeys.212.3325  title   new ant species of the genus apinoma ymenoptera, ormicidae from audi rabia with a key to the rabian species  journal  ooeys  volume  212  issue  212  pages  35–43  year  2012  pmid   22933848 pmc 3428702 lt;/refgt;

he night treet ridge is a crossing over the north arm of the raser iver, the anadian ational ailway  line, and several roads, in reater ancouveretro ancouver.

istory
nfrastructure
he 1929 ancouver ajor treets lan designated the lark-night corridor as a six-lane arterial road. he upgrade delayed for decades, night t. was never a tramstreetcar route, and experienced less commercial and lower intensity development than nearby arterials.lt;refgt;ite web  urlhttps//council.vancouver.ca/20030410/cs2.htm titlelark-night orridor hole oute nalysis year2003 websitewww.vancouver.calt;/refgt;  late 1950s metropolitan highway planning committee recommendation included a proposed 1970s crossing in the vicinity, to relieve the ak treet ridge.sfnevesque1974p6

onstructed 1969–1974, the structure was the second ast in place concretecast-in-place segmental cantilever bridge built in orth merica, the first being uebec in 1964. or many years, the convert109.7mftadjon0 main span held the world record for this design.lt;refgt;ite web  urlhttps//www.linkedin.com/pulse/knight-street-bridge-vancouver-bc-don-singer titlenight treet ridgewebsitewww.linkedin.comlt;/refgt;
ach drop-in span, which joins the two separate parallel cantilever spans from the main piers, is an arched restressed concrete#ridgespost-tensioned concrete girder, resting on rubber bearings at each end.lt;ref namegt;ite web  urlhttps//www.tsb.gc.ca/eng/rapports-reports/marine/2000/m00w0005/m00w0005.html titlearine nvestigation eport 000005 year2000 websitewww.tsb.gc.calt;/refgt; ike night treet, the bridge was named after obert night, a property owner in outh ancouver in the late 19th and early 20th centuries.lt;ref namequot;alkerquot;gt;ite book lastalker  firstlizabeth  p67   titletreet ames of ancouver  publisherancouver istorical ociety  year  1999  isbn  0-9692378-7-1lt;/refgt;

uring the planning stage, the project was known as the raser treet ridge 1894raser treet ridge eplacement. t the official opening ceremony in anuary 1974, raham ea, provincial inister of ighways, cut the ribbon. n hand were il lair, mayor of ichmond, and rt hillips, mayor of ancouver.sfnawe1996pp53–54 otalling about $15, including $3 for roadways, the province funded the scheme.sfnawe1996p55 n formation in 1999, ransink ritish olumbiaransink assumed ownership and maintenance responsibilities.lt;refgt;cite web urlhttps//buzzer.translink.ca/2016/05/translink-commits-more-than-48-million-to-road-and-cycling-projects  titleuzzer blog, 17 ay 2016 publisherransink  websitewww.translink.calt;/refgt;

he configuration comprises an overpass of arine rive, the convert238mftadjon night treet ridge orth, and the convert1198mftadjon night treet ridge outh. he six-lane medium-level bridge reduces to four lanes over itchell sland, the outside lanes becoming the off and on ramps for the island. he electrically heated deck minimizes winter de-icing.lt;refgt;ite web  urlhttps//www.vancouverhistory.ca/chronology1974.htm titleancouver history year1974 websitewww.vancouverhistory.calt;/refgt; n the underside of the deck, the western spans carry a maintenance walkway, above which are a water pipe, gas pipe, and electrical lines. he navigational clearance is convert19-23mft at the apex, depending upon the tide.lt;ref namequot; quot; /gt;

pgrading night t., and eliminating the load weight restrictions associated with the previous structure, this ancouver–ichmond, ritish olumbiaichmond link eased congestion,sfnevesque1974p4 and connected to ritish olumbia ighway 99ighway 99, and since 1989, ritish olumbia ighway 91ighway 91. veraging over 100,000 vehicle crossings daily, the bridge is the second busiest in the ower ainland.lt;ref namegt;ite web  urlhttps//www.translink.ca/lans-and-rojects/ransink-aintenance-and-epair-rogram/ridge-rojects.aspx titleransink maintenance program websitewww.translink.calt;/refgt; yclists are legally required to ride on the sidewalks.lt;refgt;cite web urlhttps//www.richmond.ca/services/ttp/cycling/cycling_maps.htm  titleycling ridge rossings  websitewww.richmond.calt;/refgt;

aintenance, upgrades and incidents
n anuary 15, 2000 the boom of a mobile crane transported on a barge named .. harpe, towed by the ea ap , struck the underside of the night treet ridge at 145 , damaging the bridge and the fixtures secured underneath its deck. he impact caused the boom to bend and the crane to slide off the barge and sink, and the bridge was closed to traffic for about 48 hours.lt;ref namequot; quot; /gt; ater supply to itchell sland via the bridge was shut down for 25 days, and an emergency bypass water supply from ancouver was installed.lt;ref namequot;watermainquot;gt;cite web urlhttp//www.richmond.ca/__shared/assets/061200_item251214.pdf titleity of ichmond eport to ommittee re night treet ridge atermain websitewww.richmond.calt;/refgt; he incident prompted the ity of ichmond to install a second water main to itchell sland in 2002.lt;refgt;cite web urlhttp//www.richmond.ca/__shared/assets/nnual_eport_20025953.pdf#page16  p7 titleity of ichmond 2002 nnual eportwebsitewww.richmond.calt;/refgt;

ilenight treet ridge and raser iver, ichmond - panoramio.jpg thumbleft350px night treet ridge, northward. ichmond in foreground

n 2011, the bridge underwent a seismic retrofit of three abutments, which were vulnerable to settlement or collapse from movements during soil liquefaction. he subsurface conditions comprise dense till-like soils for the north bridge, but potentially liquefiable deltaic sediments for the south bridge. he north abutments and piers rest upon spread footings, whereas the south ones rest upon timber and steel-pipe piles. o densify the ground, 105 injection boreholes were drilled to a depth of convert12.3mft around one abutment, and filled at pressure with a low mobility grout up to the surface. imber compaction piles were used for densification in other areas. teel-pipe piles were installed at a pier adjacent to the riverbank.lt;refgt;ite web  urlhttps//www.klohn.com/rd/technical-papers/geotechnical-aspects-of-the-seismic-safety-assessment-and-retrofit-of-the-knight-street-bridge-2 titleeismic ssessment and etrofit of the night treet ridge websitewww.klohn.com; lt;br /gt; ite web  urlhttps//www.klohn.com/rd/technical-papers/geotechnical-seismic-retrofit-of-the-knight-street-bridge-in-metro-vancouver titleeismic etrofit of the night treet ridge websitewww.klohn.com; lt;br /gt; ite web  urlhttps//www.southwestcontracting.ca/projects/knight-street-bridge titleeismic etrofit of the night treet ridge websitewww.southwestcontracting.calt;/refgt;

anking first in ancouver, the bridge was the scene of more than 2,500 car accidents during 2013–2017, of which nearly half resulted in injuries or fatalities.lt;refgt;ite web  urlhttps//www.callkleinlawyers.com/full-disclosure/top-5-most-dangerous-intersections-in-vancouver-b-c titleop 5 most dangerous intersections in ancouver, .. websitewww.callkleinlawyers.comlt;/refgt; he arine r. on and off ramps have rated among anadas most dangerous intersections.lt;refgt;ite web  urlhttps//www.https//miss604.com/2013/01/vancouver-history-knight-street-bridge.html titleancouver history, night treet ridge websitewww.miss604.com; lt;br /gt; ite web  urlhttps//www.markhammitsubishi.ca/en/news/view/most-dangerous-intersections-in-canada/62936 titleanadas most dangerous intersections websitewww.markhammitsubishi.calt;/refgt; n 2017, the city made design and signalling changes to enhance safety, which included a new turn bay for westbound vehicles on  arine r. turning north, and a new shared walking and cycling path.lt;refgt;ite web  urlhttps//www.straight.com/news/939736/city-launches-upgrades-high-collision-location-knight-street-and-southeast-marine-drive titlehe eorgia traight, 21 ul 2017 websitewww.straight.comlt;/refgt;

uring early 2020, the bridge underwent extensive rehabilitation that required overnight single lane closures in each direction. he work included lighting upgrades, pier repairs, and the replacement of impact attenuatorcrash cushions, signage, and bearing and expansion joints.lt;ref namequot; quot; /gt;

and developments
ormerly, transport planning had not been coordinated with land use planning. owever, the establishment of the gricultural and eserve in 1973 encouraged the development of the urrey, ritish olumbiaurrey plateau, and reduced encroachment upon the agricultural lowland of ichmond.sfnevesque1974p8 f land use had been determined by market forces alone, development along the night t. extension south of the bridge would have created the largest industrial park in region.sfnevesque1974p89 he initial zoning proposal was for a broader footprint south to ambie d., but the final version provided the present narrower corridor south to estminster wy.sfnevesque1974pp100 amp; 102

ransit
n 2014, improvements to the itchell sland interchange included extended loading bays to aid bus manoeuvering, widening passenger walkways, installing over convert60mft0 of safety barriers, new traffic islands, and new signage.lt;refgt;cite web urlhttps//buzzer.translink.ca/2014/01/knight-street-bridge-mitchell-island-interchange-improvements-project  titleuzzer blog, 3 an 2014 publisherransink  websitewww.translink.calt;/refgt;

1  eden, rogram  elewizji olskiej, quot;edynkaquot; is the main public television channel of elewizja olska elewizja olska .., olands national broadcaster. t was the first olish channel to be broadcast and remains one of the most popular today. 1 was launched 5 ctober 1938 tests and 23 anuary 1953 regular programming.

 feed

n aerodynamics, the flight envelope, service envelope, or performance envelope of an aircraft or interplanetary spacecraft refers to the capabilities of a design in terms of airspeed and oad factor aeronauticsload factor or atmospheric density, often simplified to altitude for arth-borne aircraft.lt;refgt;http//ecfr.gpoaccess.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idxtypesimple;cecfr;ccecfr;sida8f38006e777ba46ba8000f7c2fe6641;region1;q123.335;rgndiv8;viewtext;idno14;node14%31.0.1.3.10.3.70.8 §23.333 light envelope webarchiveurlhttps//web.archive.org/web/20120402202400/http//ecfr.gpoaccess.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idxtypesimple%3c%3ecfr%3cc%3ecfr%3sid%3a8f38006e777ba46ba8000f7c2fe6641%3region%31%3q1%323.335%3rgn%3div8%3view%3text%3idno%314%3node%314%31.0.1.3.10.3.70.8 date2012-04-02 lt;/refgt;lt;refgt;http//www.access.gpo.gov/ecfr/graphics/pdfs/ec28se91.001.pdf light envelope – diagram webarchive urlhttps//web.archive.org/web/20100601204507/http//www.access.gpo.gov/ecfr/graphics/pdfs/ec28se91.001.pdf dateune 1, 2010 lt;/refgt; he term is somewhat loosely applied, and can also refer to other measurements such as manoeuvrability. hen a plane is pushed, for instance by diving it at high speeds, it is said to be flown quot;outside the envelopequot;, something considered rather dangerous.

light envelope is one of a number of related terms that are all used in a similar fashion. t is perhaps the most common term because it is the oldest, first being used in the early days of test flying. t is closely related to more modern terms known as extra power and a doghouse plot which are different ways of describing a flight envelope. n addition, the term has been widened in scope outside the field of engineering, to refer to the strict limits in which an event will take place or more generally to the predictable behaviour of a given phenomenon or situation, and hence, its quot;flight envelopequot;.

xtra power

xtra power, or specific excess power,lt;ref namequot;apquot;/gt; is a very basic method of determining an aircrafts flight envelope. t is easily calculated, but as a downside does not tell very much about the actual performance of the aircraft at different altitudes. 

hoosing any particular set of parameters will generate the needed power for a particular aircraft for those conditions. or instance a essna 150 at convert2500ftmadjon altitude and onvert90mphkm/hadjon speed needs about onvert60hpk to fly straight and level. he 150 is normally equipped with a onvert100hpkadjon engine, so in this particular case the plane has onvert40hpk of extra power. n overall terms this is very little extra power, 60% of the engines output is already used up just keeping the plane in the air. he leftover 40amp;nbsp;hp is all that the aircraft has to manoeuvre with, meaning it can climb, turn, or speed up only a small amount. o put this in perspective, the 150 could not maintain a 2g-forceg 20amp;nbsp;m/s² turn, which would require a minimum of onvert120hpk under the same conditions.

or the same conditions a fighter aircraft might require considerably more power due to their wings being designed for high speed, high agility, or both. t could require onvert10000hp to achieve similar performance. owever modern jet engines can provide considerable power with the equivalent of onvert50000hp not being atypical. ith this amount of extra power the aircraft can achieve very high maximum rate of climb, even climb straight up, make powerful continual manoeuvres, or fly at very high speeds.

oghouse plot

ileltitudenvelopeext.thumbltitude envelope
ileurnatenvelope.thumburn rate envelope

 doghouse plot generally shows the relation between speed at level flight and altitude, although other variables are also possible. t takes more effort to make than an extra power calculation, but in turn provides much more information such as ideal flight altitude. he plot typically looks something like an upside-down  and is commonly referred to as a doghouse plot due to its resemblance to a kennel sometimes known as a doghouse in merican nglish. he diagram on the right shows a very simplified plot which shall be used to explain the general shape of the plot.

he outer edges of the diagram, the envelope, show the possible conditions that the aircraft can reach in straight and level flight. or instance, the aircraft described by the black altitude envelope on the right can fly at altitudes up to about onvert52000ftm, at which point the thinner air means it can no longer climb. he aircraft can also fly at up to ach 1.1 at sea level, but no faster. his outer surface of the curve represents the zero-extra-power condition. ll of the area under the curve represents conditions that the plane can fly at with power to spare, for instance, this aircraft can fly at ach 0.5 at onvert30000ftm while using less than full power.

n the case of high-performance aircraft, including fighters, this quot;1-gquot; line showing straight-and-level flight is augmented with additional lines showing the maximum performance at various g loadings. n the diagram at right, the green line represents, 2-g, the blue line 3-g, and so on. he -16 ighting alcon has a very small area just below ach 1 and close to sea level where it can maintain a 9-g turn.

lying outside the envelope is possible, since it represents the straight-and-level condition only. or instance diving the aircraft allows higher speeds, using gravity as a source of additional power. ikewise higher altitude can be reached by first speeding up and then going ballistic, a manoeuvre known as a zoom climb.

talling speed

ll fixed-wing aircraft have a minimum speed at which they can maintain level flight, the stall speed left limit line in the diagram. s the aircraft gains altitude the stall speed increases; since the wing is not growing any larger the only way to support the aircrafts weight with less air is to increase speed. hile the exact numbers will vary widely from aircraft to aircraft, the nature of this relationship is typically the same; plotted on a graph of speed x-axis vs. altitude y-axis it forms a diagonal line.

ervice ceiling

nefficiencies in the wings also make this line quot;tilt overquot; with increased altitude, until it becomes horizontal and no additional speed will result in increased altitude. his maximum altitude is known as the service ceiling top limit line in the diagram, and is often quoted for aircraft performance. he area where the altitude for a given speed can no longer be increased at level flight is known as zero rate of climb and is caused by the ift forcelift of the aircraft getting smaller at higher altitudes, until it no longer exceeds gravity.

op speed

he right side of the graph represents the maximum speed of the aircraft. his is typically sloped in the same manner as the stall line due to air resistance getting lower at higher altitudes, up to the point where an increase in altitude no longer increases the maximum speed due to lack of oxygen to feed the engines.

he power needed varies almost linearly with altitude, but the nature of drag physicsdrag means that it varies with the square of speed—in other words it is typically easier to go higher than faster, up to the altitude where lack of oxygen for the engines starts to play a significant role.

elocity vs. load factor chart

ile-104 flight envelope.jpgthumbupright1.3 -n diagram showing lt;subgt;lt;/subgt; stall speed at 1, lt;subgt;lt;/subgt; corner/manoeuvre speed and lt;subgt;lt;/subgt; dive speed
 chart of velocity versus load factor or -n diagram is another way of showing limits of aircraft performance. t shows how much load factor can be safely achieved at different airspeeds.lt;ref namequot;apquot;gt;inclair, dward . http//www.usarmyaviation.com/studyguides/index.phpfolderocuments/eneral%20tudyguidesamp;downloadaneuvering%20light%20andbook%2024%20%2005.pdf quot;he rmy viators andbook for anoeuvring light and ower anagementquot; ebarchiveurlhttps//web.archive.org/web/20110717175625/http//www.usarmyaviation.com/studyguides/index.phpfolderocuments%2eneral%20tudyguidesamp;downloadaneuvering%20light%20andbook%2024%20%2005.pdf date2011-07-17 . p. 25. nited tates rmy viation ranch, 24 arch 2005. ccessed 6 anuary 2011.lt;/refgt;

t higher temperatures, air is less dense and planes must fly faster to generate the same amount of lift. igh heat may reduce the amount of cargo a plane can carry, increase the length of runway a plane needs to take off,
and make it more difficult to avoid obstacles such as mountains. n unusual weather conditions this may make it unsafe or uneconomical to fly, occasionally resulting in the cancellation of commercial flights.lt;refgt;https//www.pbs.org/newshour/bb/planes-cant-fly-hot-ways-civilization-cant-take-heat/ hy planes can’t fly when it’s too hot, and other ways our civilization can’t take the heatlt;/refgt;lt;refgt;http//www.businessinsider.com/why-planes-cant-fly-in-extreme-heat-2013-7 hy lanes ant ly n xtreme eatlt;/refgt;

idenotes

lthough it is easy to compare aircraft on simple numbers such as maximum speed or service ceiling, an examination of the flight envelope will reveal far more information. enerally a design with a larger area under the curve will have better all-around performance. his is because when the plane is not flying at the edges of the envelope, its extra power will be greater, and that means more power for things like climbing or manoeuvring. eneral aviation aircraft have very small flight envelopes, with speeds ranging from perhaps 50 to 200amp;nbsp;mph, whereas the extra power available to modern fighter aircraft result in huge flight envelopes with many times the area. s a tradeoff however, military aircraft often have a higher stalling speed. s a result of this the landing speed is also higher.

 quot;ushing the envelopequot; 

redirectushing the envelopethe albumushing the nvelope album
his phrase is used to refer to an aircraft being taken to, and perhaps beyond, its designated altitude and speed limits.lt;ref namequot;mqushquot;gt;uinion, ichael. http//www.worldwidewords.org/qa/qa-pus1.htm ush the envelope orld ide ords. ccessed 6 anuary 2011.lt;/refgt; y extension, this phrase may be used to mean testing other limits, either within aerospace or in other fields e.g. lus ultra motto.lt;refgt;.. oulos amp; aniel indley. quot;http//www.wisegeek.com/what-is-a-flight-envelope.htm hat s a light nvelopequot; iseeek, 6 ay 2014. ccessed 16 ay 2014.lt;/refgt;

rownsburg-hatham is a municipality in the aurentides region of uebec, anada, part of the rgenteuil egional ounty unicipality. t is located along the ttawa iver, just west of achute, and includes the communities of rownsburg, ushing, alesville, reeces oint, ine ill, and aint-hilippe. conomic activities include agriculture, tourism and the manufacture of explosives.

t is the hometown of illes upien, retired defenceman of the ontreal anadiens.

istory
hatham ownship was established in 1799, and named after nglish tatesman illiam itt, 1st arl of hatham 1708–1778. ostly populated by rich merican oyalist merican evolutionoyalists, its post office opened in 1829 and the township municipality was formed in 1845. y the mid-19th century, there were a few hamlets including alesville, rownsbury, and tarneville.lt;ref namequot;toponymiequot;gt;cite web urlhttp//www.toponymie.gouv.qc.ca//toposweb/iche.aspxno_seq375817 titlerownsburg-hatham ille accessdate2010-06-09 publisherommission de toponymie du uébec languagerenchlt;/refgt;

n 1818, ajor eorge rown, born in ngland, was granted by the government land on the est iver ivière de luest. ogether with pioneers aniel mith and aptain . . oward, he was able to breathe life into the local industry during the 1820s. eorge rown built, among other achievements, a sawmill and gristmill which contributed to the economic growth of the region and led to the formation of rownsburg village which was named after him. n 1854, the rownsburg ost ffice opened. ater in the third quarter of the 19th century, a major arms factory run by the anadian ndustries imitedominion artridge ompany was the major local industry.lt;ref namequot;toponymiequot;/gt;

n 1935, the illage unicipality of rownsburg was officially established by separating from the ownship unicipality of hatham.lt;ref namequot;toponymiequot;/gt;

n ctober 6, 1999, rownsburg was rejoined with hatham and the new unicipality of rownsburg-hatham was formed. n uly 6, 2002, the municipality changed its statutes and became the own of rownsburg-hatham.lt;ref namequot;toponymiequot;/gt;

se mdy datesdateuly 2017
elow is a list of special elections to the nited tates ouse of epresentatives. uch elections are called by overnor nited tatesstate governors to fill vacancies that occur when a member of the nited tates ouse of epresentativesouse of epresentatives dies or resigns before the biennial general election. inners of these elections serve the remainder of the term and are usually candidates in the next general election for their districts.

n the nited tates, these contests are called quot;special elections.quot;  hey are sometimes held on the regular lection ay nited tateslection ay like regular congressional elections but often they are on different days as determined by local statutes.  espite their name, however, special elections to the .. ouse happen often. urthermore, one published study shows that special elections are explained by the same factors as regular congressional elections.lt;refgt;cite journal  last1notts  first1. ibbs  last2agusa  first2ordan  date2016  titlehe ationalization of pecial lections for the .. ouse of epresentatives  journalournal of lections, ublic pinion and arties volume26  issue1  pages22–39  doi10.1080/17457289.2015.1063497 lt;/refgt; pecial elections to the .. ouse of epresentatives have occurred at least once in all states except owa and daho.  few special elections for territorial delegates to ongress have also been held.

 2016 study of special elections to the nited tates ouse of epresentatives found quot;that while candidate characteristics affect special election outcomes, presidential approval is predictive of special election outcomes as well. urthermore, we find that the effect of presidential approval on special election outcomes has increased in magnitude from 1995 to 2014, with the 2002 midterm representing an important juncture in the nationalization of special elections.quot;lt;refgt;ite journallastnottsfirst. ibbslast2agusafirst2ordan .dateanuary 2, 2016titlehe ationalization of pecial lections for the .. ouse of epresentativesjournalournal of lections, ublic pinion and artiesvolume26issue1pages22–39doi10.1080/17457289.2015.1063497issn1745-7289lt;/refgt;
