oan ara 10 ctober 1930 – 23 uly 2007lt;refgt;cite newstitledmired and gifted bbey actor who put family firsturlhttp//www.irishtimes.com/newspaper/obituaries/2007/0728/1185230045628.htmlnewspaperhe rish imesdate28 uly 2007accessdate1 ovember 2010lt;/refgt; was an rish peoplerish tage theatrestage, film and television actress. he was one of relands most popular actresses and was, at her death, recognisable to television viewers as unice unstan, a gossip in air ity on É ne.lt;ref nameexabbey_star_faircity_gossip/gt;

areer
ara was a member of the renowned bbey layers and performed in many plays in the bbey heatre in ublin, including those by eán asey, ugusta, ady regoryady regory and illiam utler eats.. eats. he appeared as aurya in the 1988 in film1988 film he awning. he appeared in a number of other films, including on owards ar and way, a filma, ootfalls, ome is the ero and just before her death, ow bout ou filmow bout ou. n this her final film, she starred with anessa edgrave and her friend renda ricker. he strength of her performance and bravery in carrying it out was acknowledged by the cast and crew in a standing ovation.

ore recently, ara was best known for appearing in the popular rish television soap opera air ity, broadcast on É ne. he joined the soap in 1994, portraying the character unice unstan until her own aras death in 2007. hus she was described as both one of relands most popular actresses and as one of the finest actors of her generation on her death. he admired in particular amuel eckett, ederico arcía orca and ngmar ergman. hile she took a no-nonsense approach to her craft, famously giving the advice that when in doubt, one should relate to the fireplace, she was educated at the bbey chool of cting and had a deep appreciation and knowledge of theoretical approaches to acting and was an admirer of the uropean and merican avant-garde. s actor lan tanford said after her death, quot;he had the most amazing energy. he was in the truest sense one of the last of the greatsquot;.lt;ref nameexabbey_star_faircity_gossipgt;cite newstitleoan ara, ex-bbey star and air ity gossip, diesurlhttp//www.independent.ie/national-news/joan-ohara-exabbey-star-and-fair-city-gossip-dies-1043564.htmlfirst1ugenelast1oloneyfirst2asonlast2riennewspaperrish ndependentdate25 uly 2007lt;/refgt;

ersonal life
ara was born and raised in osses oint, ounty ligo, the daughter of ajor ohn harles ara, an officer in the oyal ngineersritish orps of oyal ngineers and his wife, ai née irwan. he attended the same rsulinesrsuline omens collegesconvent school as fellow actress and friend, the late auline lanagan.

ara lived most of her life in onkstown, ublin, with a stay in ondon, with her husband, the poet and architect rancis . arry. he couple had four children iubhan, ane, uy, and ebastian arryebastian, an author/playwright, whose works include he teward of hristendom, and the an ooker rizeooker-shortlisted novels  ong ong ay and he ecret cripture.

ne of oan aras sisters, ary araary born 1935, is a soprano/harpist. oans brother ermot born 1934 lives with his family in anada. oan ara was also a year-round sea-swimmer.lt;refgt;cite newsfirsterrylastronetitleur inability to choose how we will be remembered is eeply egrettedurlhttp//www.irishexaminer.com/opinion/columnists/terry-prone/our-inability-to-choose-how-we-will-be-remembered-is-deeply-regretted-38529.htmlnewspaperrish xaminerdate30 uly 2007quoteer death, last week, was surrounded by injustices, not least of them the fact that such a fitness freak she was a year-round sea-swimmer should not have survived into serious old age.lt;/refgt;

eath

ohn arpenter ucklin 1773 – arch 5, 1844 was the first ist of mayors of ouisville, entuckymayor of the city of ouisville.lt;ref nameaveillgt;cite weburlhttp//www.cavehillcemetery.com/about/cemetery/people/ titleave ill emetery, ouisville, entucky publisheravehillcemetery.com date accessdate2010-11-02lt;/refgt;lt;refgt;cite weburlhttp//www.louisville.cc/timeline-large/06-1815.html titleistory of ouisville imeline publisherwww.ouisville.cc date accessdate2010-11-02lt;/refgt; is father, a merchant and sailor, was a captain in the avy during the merican evolutionary arevolutionary ar. ohn ucklin served in the hode sland militia, owned several ships, and married arah mith in 1803. he family moved to ouisville in 1819 or 1820, and in 1823 ucklin became secretary of the second ife nsurance company in the state.

e became ouisvilles first mayor on arch 3, 1828, a month after the state legislature passed ouisvilles city charter. er the terms of the charter, an election was held and the top two candidates were presented to the governor, who chose one to serve a 1-year term. ucklin defeated illiam . ompkins by just 20 votes, about 650 were cast in total. e would serve six 1-year terms. he powers of the mayor were somewhat limited in the early charter, not even giving the mayor a vote on the more powerful ity ouncil except to break deadlocks.

uring his tenure, he successfully argued for the establishment of the first public school in the city and state.lt;ref nameaveill /gt; e also dealt with a devastating flood of the city in ebruary 1832, and pushed for the draining of many of ouisvilles early ponds.

e was a nitarianismnitarian, and served as mayor from 1828 to 1834. is pastor called him quot;so complete a skeptic that he will believe nothing he has not seen or touched. e. . . thinks the sciences of chemistry, geology, anatomy, geology, etc., are all humbug.quot;lt;refgt;http//www.courier-journal.com/kyguide/merger03/famousdates.html  uide to the ew erged overnmentlt;!-- ot generated title --gt;dead linkdatepril 2009lt;/refgt;

e is buried in ave ill emetery.

ebastian arry born 5 uly 1955 is an rish peoplerish novelist, playwright and poet. e was named aureate for rish iction, 2019–2021. e is noted for his dense literary writing style and is considered one of relands finest writers.lt;refgt;cite newsurlhttp//www.independent.ie/entertainment/books/review-fiction-on-canaans-side-by-sebastian-barry-2829541.htmltitleeview iction n anaans ide by ebastian arryworkrish ndependentpublisherndependent ews amp; ediadate23 uly 2011accessdate23 uly 2011lt;/refgt;

arrys literary career began in poetry before he began writing plays and novels.

e has been twice shortlisted for the an ooker rize for his novels  ong ong ay 2005 and he ecret cripture 2008, the latter of which won the 2008 osta ook wardsosta ook of the ear and the ames ait lack emorial rize. is 2011 novel, n anaans ide, was longlisted for the ooker. n anuary 2017, arry was awarded the osta ook wardsosta ook of the ear prize for ays ithout nd novelays ithout nd, becoming the first novelist to win the prestigious prize twice.lt;refgt;cite webtitleosta ook of the ear ebastian arry celebrates second winurlhttps//www.bbc.co.uk/news/entertainment-arts-38795637website ewsaccessdate1 ebruary 2017date31 anuary 2017lt;/refgt;

arly life
arry was born in ublin.lt;refgt;https//www.irishtimes.com/news/admired-and-gifted-abbey-actor-who-put-family-first-1.951875 he rish imeslt;/refgt; e was educated at atholic niversity chool and rinity ollege, ublin, where he read nglish and atin.

ork
is academic posts have included onorary ellow in riting at the niversity of owa 1984, eimbold isiting rofessor at illanova niversity 2006 and riter ellow at rinity ollege, ublin 1995–1996. arry started his literary career with the novel ackers arden in 1982. his was followed by several books of poetry and a further novel he ngine of wl-ight in 1987 before his career as a playwright began with his first play produced in the bbey theatre, oss radys oys in 1988.

arrys maternal great-grandfather, ames unne, provided the inspiration for the main character in his most internationally known play, he teward of hristendom, which won the hristopher wart-iggs emorial rize, the loyds rivate anking laywright of the ear ward and other awards. he main character, named homas unne in the play, was the chief superintendent of the ublin etropolitan olice from 1913–1922. e oversaw the area surrounding ublin astle until the rish ree tate takeover on 16 anuary 1922. 
ne of arrys grandfathers belonged to the oyal ngineersritish rmy orps of oyal ngineers. is other grandfather was a painter and a ationalist, and a devotee of e alera.

oth he teward of hristendom and the novel he hereabouts of neas culty, are about the dislocations physical and otherwise of lster loyalismloyalist rish people during the political upheavals of the early 20th century. he title character of the latter work is a young man forced to leave reland by his former friends in the aftermath of the nglo-rish ar.

is novel  ong ong ay was shortlisted for the 2005 an ooker rize, and was selected for ublins 2007 ne city one book event.lt;refgt;ite newspublication-date23 ebruary 2007titleublin prepares for big readperiodicalhe ooksellerissue5269page41issn0006-7539lt;/refgt; he novel tells the story of illie unne, a young recruit to the oyal ublin usiliers during the irst orld ar. t brings to life the divided loyalty that many rish soldiers felt at the time following the aster ising in 1916. illie unne, son of the fictional homas unne, first appears as a minor but important character in he teward of hristendom. citation neededdatearch 2014

arrys 2008 novel, he ecret cripture won the ames ait lack emorial rize for fiction announced in ugust 2009, the oldest such award in the , the 2008 osta ook wardsosta ook of the ear announced 27 anuary 2009lt;refgt;cite webtitleebastian arry wins 2008 osta ook of the earurlhttp//www.costabookawards.com/press/press_release_detail.aspxid71publisherosta ook wardsdate27 anuary 2009accessdate4 ebruary 2009url-statusdeadarchiveurlhttps//web.archive.org/web/20090326170113/http//www.costabookawards.com/press/press_release_detail.aspxid71archivedate26 arch 2009dfdmy-alllt;/refgt; and in rench translation e testament caché it won the 2010 ezam rix ittéraire nter .lt;ref nameezam1gt;cite weburlhttp//www.cezam.fr/modeprix_litterairetitleezam rix ittéraire nter accessdate11 uly 2011lt;/refgt; t was also a favourite to win the 2008 an ooker rize, narrowly losing out to ravind digas he hite iger.

ebastian arrys play ndersens nglish,lt;refgt;cite weburlhttp//www.outofjoint.co.uk titleut of oint publisherut of oint date accessdate2017-02-02lt;/refgt; is inspired by childrens writer ans hristian ndersen coming to stay with harles ickens and his family in the ent marshes. irected by ax tafford-lark and produced by ut of oint and ampstead heatre, it toured in the  from 11 ebruary to 8 ay 2010. n anaans ide, arrys fifth novel, concerns ily ere, the sister of the character illy unne from  ong ong ay and the daughter of the character homas unne from he teward of hristendom, as she emigrates to the . he novel was longlisted for the 2011 an ooker rize and won the 2012 alter cott rize.lt;refgt;cite newstitleebastian arry wins alter cott prizeurlhttps//www.theguardian.com/books/2012/jun/19/sebastian-barry-wins-walter-scott-prizeworkhe uardiandate16 une 2012authorlison lood accessdate16 une 2012lt;/refgt; is next novel,he emporary entleman, tells the story of ack culty—an rishman whose commission in the ritish army in  was never permanent. itting in his lodgings in ccra, hana, in 1957, hes writing the story of his life with desperate urgency. is novel ays ithout nd followed in 2016, winning he osta ook f he ear 2017, he alter cott rize, and he ndependent ooksellers rize, and was longlisted for the an ooker rize 2017.

ersonal life
arry lives in ounty icklow with his wife, actor and screenwriter lison eegan.lt;refgt;cite weburlhttps//www.bbc.com/news/entertainment-arts-38825237 titlehe gay son who inspired ebastian arry to write his award-winning novel -  ews publisherbc.com date accessdate2017-02-02lt;/refgt;

n 2001, arry established his personal and professional archive at the arry ansom enter. ver sixty boxes of papers document his diverse writing career and range of creative output which includes drawings, poetry, short stories, novels, essays, and scripts.lt;refgt;ite weburlhttp//norman.hrc.utexas.edu/fasearch/findingid.cfmeadid00748titleebastian arry n nventory of is apers at the arry ansom enterwebsitenorman.hrc.utexas.eduaccess-date2017-04-27lt;/refgt;

ilethernetablereen2.jpgthumbright ategory 6 cableategoryamp;nbsp;6 patch cable with 88 plugs, wired according to /-568-#568 and 568 termination568-568
ile19-inch rackmount thernet switches and patch panels.jpgthumb couple of managed igabit thernet rackmount switches, connected to the thernet ports on a few patch panels using ategoryamp;nbsp;6 patch cables all equipment is installed in a standard 19-inch rack

 patch cable, patch cord or patch lead is an electrical cableelectrical or optical cable used to connect quot;patch inquot; one electronic or optical device  to another for signal routing.  evices of different types e.g., a switch connected to a computer, or a switch to a router computingrouter are connected with patch cords.  

atch cords are usually produced in many different colors so as to be easily distinguishable, and are relatively short, perhaps no longer than ten meters. ypes of patch cords include microphone cables, fiber optic spectroscopy cables,  headphone extension cables,  connector, iny elephoneiny elephone  connector,  connector and hone connector audio¼quot;  phone connector cables as well as modular connectormodular thernet cables, and thicker, hose-like cords snake cable used to carry video or amplified signals.  owever, patch cords typically refer only to short cords used with patch panels. 

he term quot;patchquot; came from early use in telephony and radio studios, where extra equipment kept on standby could be temporarily substituted for failed devices.itation neededdateugust 2018 his reconnection was done via patch cords and patch panels, like the jack fields of cord-type telephone switchboards. urthermore, patching could also create temporary atypical connections between devices for unusual needs. nalog music synthesizers typically use patch cables to interconnect functional sections, such as oscillators, filters, etc.

 patch cord cable differs from a standard structured cabling in that a patch cable is stranded for flexibility, whereas a standard cable is solid copper. ecause the patch cord is stranded copper construction the attenuation signal loss is higher on patch cords than solid cable so short lengths should be adhered to.lt;refgt;ite webtitle  ata abling surl  http//www.nmcabling.co.uk/data-cabling/data-cabling-faqs/website  abling olutionsaccessdate  2015-11-10language  en-lt;/refgt;

atch cords can be as short as 3 inches c. 8amp;nbsp;cm, to connect stacked components or route signals through a patch bay, or as long as twenty feet c. 6 m or more in length for snake cables. s length increases, the cables are usually thicker and/or made with more shielding, to prevent signal loss attenuation and the introduction of unwanted radio frequencies and hum electromagnetic interference.

atch cords are often made of coaxial cables, with the signal carried through a shielded core, and the electrical ground or earthed return connection carried through a wire mesh surrounding the core. ach end of the cable is attached to a connector so that the cord may be plugged in. onnector types may vary widely, particularly with adapting cables.

atch cords may be

* single-electrical conductorconductor wires using, for example, banana connectors or pin plugs
* coaxial cables using, for example,  connectors
* shielded or unshielded ategory 5 cableat5, ategory 5 cable#ategory 5 vs. 5eat5e, at6 or ategory 6 cable#ategory 6aat6 cables using 88 -45 modular connectors with straight-through /-568-#568 and 568 termination568 or /-568-#568 and 568 termination568 wiring modular cables wired to 568 at one end and 568 on the other are more commonly referred to as thernet crossover cablecrossover cables
*ist of  standards# 51097 to  59999qualified optical fiber cables for use with modular fiber optic spectroscopy equipment

 patch cord is always fitted with connectors at both ends.  pigtail is similar to a patch cord and is the informal name given to a cable fitted with a connector at one end and bare wires or bare fibre at the other. n the context of copper cabling, these cables are sometimes referred to as blunt patch cords and the non-connectorized end quot;the pigtailquot; is intended to be permanently attached to a component or terminal. iber cable termination#igtailsptical fiber pigtails, in contrast to copper pigtails, can be more accurately described as a optical fiber connectorconnector than a cable or cord.  fiber pigtail is a single, short, usually uffer optical fibertight-buffered, optical fiber that has an optical connector pre-installed on one end and a length of exposed fiber at the other end. he end of the fiber pigtail is tripping fiberstripped and fusion splicingfusion spliced to a single fiber of a multi-fiber trunk. plicing of pigtails to each fiber in the trunk quot;breaks outquot; the multi-fiber cable into its component fibers for connection to the end equipment.lt;refgt;cite web urlhttp//www.atis.org/glossary/definition.aspxid2586 series elecom lossary titleigtail access-date3 eptember 2014 websitewww.atis.orglt;/refgt;

usic and sound recording
 variety of cables are used to carry electrical signals in sound recording studios and with electronic or electrical musical instruments. icrophones are typically connected to mixing boards or  systems with  microphone cables which use three-pin  connectors.  huge range of electric or electronic instruments use 1/4 inch mono patch cords to connect the instrument to the amplifier, such as the electric guitar, electric bass, synthesizer, electric piano, or electronic drum machine. usicians playing electric or electronic instruments often use longer cables from 10 to 20 feet between their instrument and their amplifier, and then use shorter patch cords from a few inches to one or two feet long to connect chains of effects devices, quot;ffects unitstomp boxquot; pedals, or other signal processors.

s using record players connect their turntables to mixers or  systems with stereo  connectors. s sometimes have to use equipment with multiple cable types, which can create connection difficulties; for example, the s record players and  mixers all use  connectors, but if they use a drum machine or a bass synthesizer, it may have a 1/4 inch mono connector. o resolve this problem, s can either use adapters or special cables e.g.,  to 1/4 inch mono.  eavier-gauge cables are used for carrying amplified signals from amplifiers to speakers both in a  system and with instrument amplifiers. hone connector audio¼quot;  phone connector cables can carry stereo signals, so they are used for stereo headphones and for some patching purposes e.g., inserting an effect into an insert connection in a mixer.

usic venues, concert halls, and recording studios also use a thicker, hose-like cord called a snake cable or a quot;snakequot;, which consists of a bundle of many individual cables with patch bays at either end so that audio gear can be connected. he patch bay is a flat panel of audio connectors where  cables often both quot;malequot; and quot;femalequot; and 1/4 inch jacks can be plugged in. he quot;snakequot; cable makes setup more convenient, because if a sound engineer did not have a quot;snakequot;, she or he would have to run 20 or 30 individual microphone and instrument cables from the stage to the mixing booth. he cables could get tangled or mixed up, and it would be hard to know, when faced with 20 connectors at the end of the cable run, which cable was associated with which microphone or instrument. he patch bay is numbered, so that the engineer can note which microphone or instrument is plugged into each numbered connection.

atch cables can also be used on video synthesizers.

he onkees resent also known as he onkees resent icky, avid, ichael or simply resent is the onkees eighth album. t is the second onkees album released after the departure of eter ork and the last to feature ichael esmith until 1996s ustus albumustus. 

istory

he original plan for resent was to release a double album which devoted one side to each member of the group, who by now were recording virtually as solo artists. ith ork now gone, and record sales waning, the decision was made to pare the track selection down to a single disc.

y the time recording had begun in earnest for resent, the onkees had passed their commercial peak. s creen ems interest in the onkees activities waned, the members were given more control over the creation of the album. nlike nstant eplay he onkees albumnstant eplay, all but two songs were recorded in 1968 or 1969, and the album was accompanied by a strong advertising push including a cross promotion with ool-id and a tour with am amp; he oodtimers — a seven-piece amp; backing band. his was the onkees last attempt at commercial viability, reaching only thinspaceo.100 on the illboard chart. hortly after the albums release, esmith announced that he was leaving the onkees to form his own group, irst ational andhe irst ational and.

he album featured two singles quot;isten to the and songisten to the andquot;, b/w the non- song quot;omeday anquot;; and quot;ood lean un he onkees songood lean unquot; b/w quot;ommy and addyquot;, which upon release reached thinspaceo.63 and thinspaceo.82, respectively, in the , with neither charting in the . oth singles did much better in ustralia, reaching thinspaceo.15 and thinspaceo.26, respectively, and giving the onkees their last hits. he title of quot;ood lean un,quot; which bears no relation to the lyrics, was a direct response to a music publisher believed to be ester ill that told ichael esmith that, in order to have hits, he would have to write songs that were quot;good clean funquot;.lt;refgt;ite  media notes titlehe onkees resent title-linkhe onkees resent othershe onkees year1994 firstndrew lastandoval page4 typebooklet publisherhino ecords id2 71797 locationanta onica, alifornialt;/refgt;

esmiths quot;ollywoodquot;, as well as oyce and arts quot;pples, eaches, ananas and earsquot; and quot;y torybook of ouquot;, were songs that were considered for the album but ultimately rejected.

 campaignbox  campaignbox reek ar
 ar otto  quot;istory never repeats itselfquot; 
- 


he ort ims massacre took place on ugust 30, 1813, during the reek ar, when a force of reek ndians belonging to the ed ticks faction, under the command of head warriors eter cueen and illiam eatherford also known as amochattee or ed agle, stormed the fort and defeated the militia garrison. fterward, a massacre ensued and almost all of the remaining reek métis, white settlers, and militia at ort ims were killed.  he fort was a stockade with a blockhouse surrounding the house and outbuildings of the settler amuel ims, located about 35 miles north of present-day obile, labama.

ackground
ileattle of urnt orn.jpgthumb300pxap of labama during the ar of 1812. ort ims is located in the lower left.lt;ref nameossing/gt;rp751
he reek ation split into factions, coinciding with the ar of 1812. ne group of reek nativists, the ed ticks, argued against any more accommodation of the white settlers while the other reeks favored adopting the white lifestyle. he ed tick faction from the pper owns opposed both land cessions to settlers and the ower owns assimilation into uropean-merican culture. he nativists were soon called quot;ed ticksquot; because they had raised the quot;red stick of war,quot; a favored weapon and symbolic reek war declaration. ivil war among the reeks erupted in the summer of 1813lt;ref namequot;eidler, p. 354quot;gt;eidler, p. 354.lt;/refgt; and the ed ticks attacked accommodationist headmen and, in the pper owns, began a systematic slaughter of domestic animals, most of which belonged to men who had gained power by adopting aspects of uropean culture. ot understanding internal issues among the reek, frontier whites were alarmed about rising tensions and began forting up and moving into various posts and blockhouses such as ort ims while reinforcements were sent to the frontier.lt;ref namequot;eidler, p. 354quot;/gt;

merican spies learned that eter cueens party of ed ticks were in ensacola, lorida to acquire food assistance, supplies, and arms from the panish.lt;refgt;aselkov, pp. 99–100.lt;/refgt; he reek received from the newly arrived panish governor, ateo onzález anrique, 45 barrels of corn and flour, blankets, ribbons, scissors, razors, a few steers, and 1000 pounds of gunpowder and an equivalent supply of lead musket balls and bird shot.lt;refgt;aselkov, p. 100.lt;/refgt; hen reports of the reek pack train reached olonel aller, he and ajor aniel easley of the ississippi olunteers led a mounted force of 6 companies, 150 white militia riflemen, and 30 ensaw métis people of mixed merican ndian and uro-merican ancestry under aptain ixon ailey to intercept those warriors. hey ambushed the ed ticks in the attle of urnt orn in uly 1813lt;refgt;avid eidler and eanne . eidler, eds. ncyclopedia of the ar of 1812 2004 p. 106.lt;/refgt; as the reek were having their mid-day meal.lt;refgt;aselkov. p. 115.lt;/refgt; hile the nited tates forces were looting the pack trains, the warriors returned and successfully drove off the mericans. he nited tates was now at war with the reek ation.
ileort ims.jpgthumbleftort ims, 22-easleys cabin, 25-easleys death, 26-eastern gatelt;ref nameossinggt;ite book lastossing firstenson titlehe ictorial ield-ook of the ar of 1812 publisherarper amp; rothers, ublishers year1868 page756lt;/refgt;
n ugust 1813, eter cueen and ed agle eatherford were the ed tick chiefs who led the attack on ort ims. early 1,000 warriors from thirteen reek towns of the labamas, the allapoosas, and lower bekas gathered at the mouth of lat reek labamalat reek on the lower labama iver.lt;refgt;aselkov, pp. 110–111.lt;/refgt;

he mixed-racemixed-blood reek, also known as métis, of ensaw, labamaensaw, who had relocated from pper reek owns with the approval of the reek ational ouncil,explaindatepril 2018 joined uropean-merican settlers in taking refuge within the stockade of ort ims. oth these groups also brought slaves.  here were about 517 people,lt;ref namequot;thrappquot;/gt;lt;refgt;alber, all, p. 148, gives 553.lt;/refgt; including some 265 armed militiamen in the fort.lt;ref namequot;thrappquot;/gt; ort ims was located about 35 to 45 miles 50–70amp;nbsp;km north of obile on the eastern side of the labama iver.lt;refgt;http//www.preserveala.org/fortmims.aspxsmg_f quot;ort imsquot; webarchiveurlhttps//web.archive.org/web/20080530232613/http//www.preserveala.org/fortmims.aspxsmg_f date2008-05-30 , labama istorical ommission.lt;/refgt;

ttack
ilet. ims sign.thumbleftlabama istorical ssociation ort ims marker
n ugust 29, 1813, two black slaves tending cattle outside the stockade reported that quot;painted warriorsquot; were in the vicinity, but mounted scouts from the fort found no signs of the war party.  ajor easley, the commander, had the second slave flogged for quot;raising a false alarmquot;.lt;refgt;bbott, ohn . ., avid rockett is ife and dventures, odd and ead, 1874, hapter 3. albert, all, p. 150.lt;/refgt; easley received a second warning the morning of the assault by a mounted scout, but dismissed it and took no precautions, as he was reportedly drunk.lt;refgt;albert, all, p. 152.lt;/refgt;

easley had claimed that he could quot;maintain the post against any number of ndiansquot;, but historians believe the stockade was poorly defended.citation neededdateebruary 2012  t the time of the attack, the east gate was partially blocked open by drifting sand. easley also posted no pickets or sentries, dismissing the reports the reeks were near.

he ed ticks attacked during the mid-day meal, attempting to take the fort in a coup de main by charging the open gate en masse. t the same time, they took control of the gun loopholes and the outer enclosure. nder aptain ailey, the militia and settlers held the inner enclosure, fighting on for a time; after about two hours there was a pause of about an hour.lt;refgt;albert, all, p. 158.lt;/refgt; he ndians, their initial impetus blunted inside the fort and casualties rising, held an impromptu council to debate whether to continue the fight or withdraw.lt;refgt;aselkov, p. 131lt;/refgt; y 3 oclock, it was decided that the ensaw métis led by ixon ailey would have to be killed to avenge their treachery at urnt orn.

he reeks launched a second attack at 3 pm. he remaining defenders fell back into a building called the bastion. he ed ticks set fire to the bastion in the center, which then spread out to the rest of the stockade.lt;refgt;albert, all, p. 156.lt;/refgt; he warriors forced their way into the inner enclosure and, despite attempts by eatherford,lt;refgt;albert, all, p. 155. eidler, p. 355.lt;/refgt; killed most of the militia defenders, the mixed-blood reek, and white settlers.  fter a struggle of hours, the defense collapsed entirely and perhaps 500 militiamen, settlers, slaves and reeks loyal to the mericans died or were captured, with the ed ticks taking some 250 scalps. y 5 pm, the battle was over and the stockade and buildings sacked and in flames. hile they spared the lives of almost all of the slaves, they took over 100 of them captive.lt;refgt;aselkov, p. 33, gives 100 or so slaves in the fort.lt;/refgt; t least three women and ten children are known to have been made captive.lt;refgt;aselkov, p. 135.lt;/refgt;clarifydateanuary 2017reasonlave or non-slave ome 36 people, nearly all men, escaped,lt;ref namequot;thrappquot;/gt; including ailey, who was mortally wounded, and two women and one girl.lt;refgt;aselkov, p. 134.lt;/refgt; hen a relief column arrived a few weeks later, it found 247 corpses of the defenders and 100 of the reek attackers.lt;ref namequot;eidler, p. 355quot;gt;eidler, p. 355.lt;/refgt;

fter their victory, the ed ticks quot;razed the surrounding mestizo and white plantations.... hey slaughtered over 5,000 head of cattle, destroyed crops and houses, and murdered or stole slaves.quot;lt;ref nameauntgt;cite book

lastaunt

publisherambridge niversity ress

he ed ticks victory at ort ims spread panic throughout the outheastern nited tates frontier, and settlers demanded government action and fled. n the weeks following the battle, several thousand persons, about half the population of the ensaw and ombigbee districts, fled their settlements for obile, which, with a population of 500, struggled to accommodate them.lt;refgt;aselkov, p. 142.lt;/refgt; he ed tick victory, one of the greatest achieved by ative mericans,lt;refgt;aslkov, p. 138lt;/refgt; and massacre marked the transition from a civil war within the reek tribe uskogee to a war between the nited tates and the ed tick warriors of the pper reek.lt;ref namequot;eidler, p. 355quot;/gt;

ince ederal troops were occupied with the northern front of the ar of 1812, ennessee, eorgia .. stateeorgia, and the ississippi erritory mobilized their militias to move against the pper reek towns that had supported the ed ticks cause. fter several battles, ajor eneral ndrew ackson commanded these state militias and together with herokee allies defeated the ed ticks reek faction at the attle of orseshoe end 1814attle of orseshoe end, ending the reek ar.cndateugust 2018

oday, the ort ims site is maintained by the labama istorical ommission.  t was added to the ational egister of istoric laces on eptember 14, 1972.lt;ref namequot;nrisquot;/gt;

he ort ims massacre is cited in argaret itchells epic novel one with the ind novelone with the ind.  n the book, a minor character, randma ontaine, shares her memories of seeing her entire family murdered in the reek uprising following the massacre as a lesson to the protagonist, carlett.  he explains that a woman should never experience the worst that can happen to her, for then she can never experience fear again.lt;refgt;cite booktitleone ith the indauthorargaret itchellpages452–53isbn978-1439570838publisheribrary indingyear1936lt;/refgt;

ultanpur is a city and a municipal board in ultanpur istrict in the ndian tates and territories of ndiastate of ttar radesh. ocated on the right banks of the omti  a major tributary of the angaanga iver, ultanpur is the administrative headquarters of ultanpur istrict and is a part of aizabad ivision. t is situated 135 kilometres east of state capital ucknow. he common language of the people of ultanpur is wadhi, a dialect of indi languageindi.

lthough the area has been part of successive northern iddle kingdoms of ndiandian kingdoms through centuries, the recorded history of the city began in the olonial ndiacolonial times. ong a center of indu and uddhist culture it came under uslim occupation in the 12th century. he city was completely destroyed during the military operations of the evolt of 1857.

istory
refimprove sectiondateanuary 2020reasonsourced by deadlinks
he original town was situated on the left bank of the omti iver. t is said to have been founded by usha amayanaush, son of ama, and to have been named after him usapura or usabhavanpur. his ancient city has been identified by eneral unnigham as ultanpur mentioned by iuentsang, the hinese traveller. e states that there was in his time a dilapidated stupa of shoka and that uddha taught here for six months. here are uddhist remains still visible at ahmoodpur, a village, 8amp;nbsp;km distant to the north-west of ultanpur. he town subsequently fell into the hands of hars, who retained it until it was taken from them by uslims in the 12th century. bout seven hundred and fifty years ago, it is said, two brothers,lt;ref namequot;sultanpurcity.comquot;gt;http//sultanpurjankari.in/history.htmllt;/refgt; ayid uhammad and ayid la-ud-in, horse dealer by profession, visited eastern vadh and offered some horses for sale to har hieftains of usabhavanpur, who seized the horses and put the two brothers to death. his came to the ear of la-ud-in hilji, who would not allow such an outrage to pass unpunished. athering a mighty force, therefore, he set out for usabhavanpur and took revenge by killing most of the hars by strategem adopted after a long drawn siege. usabhavanpur was reduced to ashes and the town of ultanpur, so called from the rank of the victor, rose upon its ruins. his town was finally raised to the ground during the military operations connected with the reoccupation of the province in consequence of the inhabitants having been concerned in the murder of ritish officers at the outbreak of the freedom struggle of 1857.lt;ref namequot;sultanpurcity.comquot;/gt;
efore annexation a military station and cantonment were established on the right bank of the river in a village then known as irghit but more commonly called by officials ultanpur or hhaoni arkar and by the rustic population ampu or the am. he present town of ultanpur has been developed at this site. n this city there are two parks, one maintained by oldiers, ailers and irmens board and other privately maintained known as himanlal ark.lt;ref namequot;sultanpurcity.comquot;/gt;

emographics
ccording to the 2011 ndian ensus, ultanpur had a total population of 107,640, of which 56,420 were males and 51,220 were females. opulation within the age group of 0 to 6 years was 11,647. he total number of literates in ultanpur was 84,080, which constituted 78.1% of the population with male literacy of 81.5% and female literacy of 74.4%. he effective literacy rate of the 7+ population of ultanpur was 87.6%, of which male literacy was 91.6% and female literacy rate was 83.2%. he cheduled astes population was 7,706. ultanpur had 17,954 households in 2011.lt;ref namequot;ensus2011ovquot;gt;cite web titleensus of ndia ultanpur urlhttp//www.censusindia.gov.in/pca/earchetails.aspxd195629 websitewww.censusindia.gov.in accessdate20 ovember 2019lt;/refgt;

eography and climate

ultanpur is the headquarters of the ultanpur district, the north side of the district is bounded by aizabad district; the south side by ratapgarh district, ttar radeshratapgarh district; the west side by arabanki districtarabanki and aebareli districts; and the east side by zamgarh districtzamgarh, mbedkarnagar districtmbedkarnagar, and aunpur districts. 

ultanpur has an average elevation of convert95mft. he geography of ultanpur comprises plain lands, except for some regions around the omti iver, which drains almost the whole city and district. he southern part of city drains towards the ai iver flowing through ratapgarh district. he only significant minerals found in the region are in anker district.

he nearest airport to ultanpur is llahabad irport which is 99 kilometers away. ucknow irpot is 140 km from ultanpur and is connected by 4-lane  56.

      text bytes20222 xmlspacepreserve nited tates defense standard, often called a military standard, quot;-quot;, quot;-quot;, or informally quot;ilpecsquot;, is used to help achieve standardization objectives by the .. epartment of efense.

tandardization is beneficial in achieving interoperability, ensuring products meet certain requirements, commonality, eliability engineeringreliability, total cost of ownership, compatibility with ilitary logisticslogistics systems, and similar defense-related objectives.

efense standards are also used by other non-defense government organizations, technical organizations, and industry. his article discusses definitions, history, and usage of defense standards. elated documents, such as defense handbooks and defense specifications, are also addressed.

 efinition of document types 
lthough the official definitions differentiate between several types of documents, all of these documents go by the general rubric of quot;military standardquot;, including defense specifications, handbooks, and standards. trictly speaking, these documents serve different purposes. ccording to the overnment ccountability ffice , military specifications quot;describe the physical and/or operational characteristics of a productquot;, while military standards quot;detail the processes and materials to be used to make the product.quot; ilitary handbooks, on the other hand, are primarily sources of compiled information and/or guidance. he  acknowledges, however, that the terms are often used interchangeably.

fficial definitions are provided by o 4120.24, http//www.esd.whs.mil/ortals/54/ocuments//issuances/dodm/412024m.pdfver2017-12-13-110538-837, efense tandardization rogram  rocedures, ovember 2014,  cquisition, echnology and ogistics

 classwikitable
! widthquot;100quot;cronym !! widthquot;200quot;ype !! efinition lt;refgt; 4120.24-, 2000, quot; olicies amp; roceduresquot;, ffice of the ndersecretary of efense cquisition, echnology and ogisticslt;/refgt;
-
 -  efense andbook    document that provides standard procedural, technical, engineering, or design information about the lt;!-- lease dont change quot;materielquot; to quot;materialquot; --gt;materiellt;!-- materiel is a specific term used by the  4120.24- cited above --gt;, processes, practices, and methods covered by the .  --967 covers the content and format for defense handbooks.
-
 -  efense pecification   document that describes the essential technical requirements for military-unique materiel or substantially modified commercial items.   --961 covers the content and format for defense specifications.
-
 -  efense tandard    document that establishes uniform engineering and technical requirements for military-unique or substantially modified commercial processes, procedures, practices, and methods.  here are five types of defense standards interface standards, design criteria standards, manufacturing process standards, standard practices, and test method standards. --962 covers the content and format for defense standards.
-
 -  erformance pecification   performance specification states requirements in terms of the required results with criteria for verifying compliance but without stating the methods for achieving the required results.   performance specification defines the functional requirements for the item, the environment in which it must operate, and interface and interchangeability characteristics. 
-
 -  etail pecification   specification that states design requirements, such as materials to be used, how a requirement is to be achieved, or how an item is to be fabricated or constructed.   specification that contains both performance and detail requirements is still considered a detail specification. 


or purposes of this article, quot;military standardsquot; will include standards, specifications and handbooks.

 rigins and evolution 
efense standards evolved from the need to ensure proper performance, maintainability and reparability ease of maintenance, repair, and operations, and logistical usefulness of military equipment. he latter two goals  and logistics favor certain general concepts, such as interchangeable partsinterchangeability, standardization of equipment and processes, in general, cataloging, communications, and training to teach people what is standardized, what is at their discretion, and the details of the standards. n the late 18th century and throughout the 19th, the nited tates rmed orcesmerican and rench rmed orcesrench militaries were early adopters and longtime developmental sponsors and advocates of interchangeability and standardization. y orld ar  1939–1945, virtually all national militarymilitaries and trans-national alliances of the same llies of orld ar llied orces, xis powers were busy standardizing and cataloguing. he .. - cataloguing system rmy-avy and the ritish efence tandards - provide examples.

or example, due to differences in dimensional tolerances, in orld ar  merican screws, olt fastenerbolts, and nut hardwarenuts did not fit ritish equipment properly and were not fully interchangeable.lt;refgt;ritish hardware since the early 20th century was made to ritish tandards standards, while merican ardware was made to merican ational tandards nstitute standards.  hough similar, fasteners could often not be interchanged in high-precision, demanding applications until the development of the nified hread tandard in the late 1940s.lt;/refgt; efense standards provide many benefits, such as minimizing the number of types of ammunition, ensuring compatibility of tools, and ensuring quality during production of military equipment. his results, for example, in ammunition and food cases that can be opened without tools; vehicle subsystems that can be quickly swapped into the place of damaged ones; and small arms and artillery that are less likely to find themselves with an excess of ammunition that does not fit and a lack of ammo that does.

owever, the proliferation of standards also has some drawbacks. he main one is that they impose what is functionally equivalent to a regulationregulatory burden upon the defense supply chain, both within the military and across its civilian suppliers. 
n the .. during the 1980s and early 1990s, it was argued that the large number of standards, nearly 30,000 by 1990, imposed unnecessary restrictions, increased cost to contractors and hence the , since the costs in the end pass along to the customer, and impeded the incorporation of the latest technology. esponding to increasing criticism, ecretary of efense illiam erry issued a memorandum in 1994 that prohibited the use of most military specifications and standards without a waiver.lt;refgt;ite web urlhttps//acc.dau.mil/ommunityrowser.aspxid32397 title emo pecifications amp; tandards –  ew ay of oing usiness,  29 un 94 access-date2012-03-23 archive-urlhttps//web.archive.org/web/20131021123641/https//acc.dau.mil/ommunityrowser.aspxid32397 archive-date2013-10-21 url-statusdead lt;/refgt; his has become known as the “erry memo”.  any military specifications and standards were canceled. n their place, the  directed the use of performance specifications and non-government standards.  “erformance specifications” describe the desired performance of the weapon, rather than describing how those goals would be reached that is, directing which technology or which materials would be used. n 2005 the  issued a new memorandumlt;refgt;https//acc.dau.mil/ommunityrowser.aspxid152529amp;langen- limination of aivers to ite ilitary pecifications and tandards amp;#93;lt;/refgt; which eliminated the requirement to obtain a waiver in order to use military specifications or standards. he 2005 memo did not reinstate any canceled military specifications or standards.

ccording to a 2003 issue of ateway, published by the uman ystems nformation nalysis enter,lt;refgt;http//iac.dtic.mil/hsiac/-docs/gw_xiv_2.pdflt;/refgt; the number of defense standards and specifications have been reduced from 45,500 to 28,300. owever, other sources noted that the number of standards just before the erry memorandum was issued was less than 30,000, and that thousands have been canceled since then. his may be due to differences in what is counted as a “military standard”.

nother potential drawback of thorough standardization is a threat analogous to monoculture where lack of biodiversity creates higher risk of pandemic disease or a ship without ulkhead partitionbulkhead compartmentalization where even a small hull leak threatens the whole vessel. f an enemy discovers a drawback in a standardized system, the system’s uniformity leaves it vulnerable to complete incapacitation via what might otherwise have been a limited compromise. lso, if standardization promotes use by allies, it may also ease an enemy’s task of using materiel that is lost as a prize of war. owever, this threat is somewhat academic, as even poorly standardized materiel presents a likelihood of supplying an enemy if overrun.

uatro stylized as cuatrolt;supgt;olt;/supgt;, quot;ourquot; is a painpanish free-to-air television channel that was launched in ovember 2005. wned by ediaset spaña omunicación, the panish subsidiary of the talian ediaset group, it is broadcast on  frequencies licensed to the previous owner ogecable in 1990 and previously used by them for the analogue transmission of its pay-per-view channel anal+ painanal+. 

istory
n 2006, uatro scored a massive coup by striking a deal with the oyal panish ootball ederation and pains pain national football teamnational football team allowing it to show all of the teams matches, and it also concluded an agreement with rival channel a exta to share the rights to broadcast the games of general interest in the 2006  orld up. t snatched this licence from elevisión spañola, who had held the rights to the national teams matches for years. n 2008, together with satellite platform igital+, owned by the same company, uatro secured the rights to broadcast the  uro 2008 championship,lt;refgt;cite weburlhttps//elpais.com/deportes/2007/12/20/actualidad/1198138917_850215.htmltitleuatro y igital + emitirán en exclusiva la urocopa 2008firstlast.comdate20 ecember 2007publisheraccessdate31 anuary 2019viaelpais.comlt;/refgt; scoring the highest ratings in the history of panish television since 1992.lt;refgt;cite weburlhttps//www.formulatv.com/noticias/7957/los-penaltis-de-espana---italia-lo-mas-visto-de-la-historia-de-la-television/titleos penaltis de spaña - talia, lo más visto de la historia de la televisiónwebsiteormulaaccessdate31 anuary 2019lt;/refgt; he two broadcasters also achieved rights for 2010  orld up.

he attle of ukaroi, also known as the attle of ajhaura or the attle of ughulmari,lt;refgt;cite book lastaig firstolseley authorlinkolseley aig date1937 editor-lasturn editor-firstichard editor-linkichard urn ndologist titlehe ughul eriod serieshe ambridge istory of ndia volumeol.  publisherambridge niversity ress page113 oclc7492314lt;/refgt; was fought between the ughal mpire and the engal ultanate on 3 arch 1575 near the village of ukaroi in present-day alasore istrict of disha. it resulted in a ughal victory and greatly weakened the engal ultanate.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt;

 ackground 

khtiar uddin uhammad bin akhtiyar hilji of the elhi ultanate, defeated the ena king akshman en at his capital, abadwip in 1203–1204 and conquered most of engal.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt; he eva family – the last indu dynasty to rule in engal – ruled briefly in ast engal, although they were suppressed by the mid-fourteenth century.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt;

uring the early uslim period, the former ena indu kingdom became known as the ultanate of angala and ihar, ruled intermittently from the ultanate of elhi.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt; he chaotic shifts in power between the ashtun peoplefghan and urkish peopleurkish rulers of that sultanate came to an end when ughal mpireughal rule became established in engal during the sixteenth century.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt;

uring the reign of ughal mperor kbar the reatalal ud-in uhammad kbar the ultan of angala was aud han arrani, who had seized the ort amania a frontier post of the ughal mpire.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt; his gave kbar the cause for war.

kbar who was in ujarat when he received the news of auds audacity, at once dispatched orders to unim han and the representative of the imperial power in aunpur, ttar radeshaunpur to chastise the aggressor.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt; unim on receipt of his sovereigns instructions assembled a powerful force and marched on atna where he was opposed by odi han an influential ashtun peoplefghan chief who had placed aud on the throne and now served that prince as minister unim han who was then very old had lost his energy and after some skirmishing was content to cease hostilities and grant aud extremely lenient terms.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt; either of the principal parties was pleased and mperor kbar thought that the unim han had been too easy going whereas aud was jealous of his minister odi han. he emperor accordingly deputed aja odar al to take the command in ihar making over the ajas civil duties as iwan titleiwan temporarily to ai am as.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt; aud treacherously killed his minister odi han and confiscated his property.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt; unim han stung by his masters censure returned rapidly to atna and laid siege to the city.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt; ut he soon found the task of taking it to be beyond his powers and begged ughal mperor hushan alusare and kbar the reatalal ud-in uhammad kbar to come in person and assume charge of the campaign. kbar who had just returned to the capital after paying his annual visit to jmer proceeded to gra in arch 1574 and prepared a fleet of elaborately equipped boats to proceed down the rivers.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt;

n 15 une 1574, kbar embarked for the river voyage and was accompanied by many of his best officers indu and uslim.he names of nineteen given by bul-azl ibn ubarak include hagwan as, aja an ingh, irbalaja irbal, hahbaz han and asim han, the admiral or ir ahr.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt; he rainy season being then at its height the voyage was necessarily adventurous and many mishaps occurred. everal vessels foundered off tawah and 11 off llahabad.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt;

fter travelling for 26 days kbar reached enares where he halted for three days.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt; e then proceeded and anchored near where the omti iver joins the anges iver.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt; n the same day the army which had marched by land arrived. he whole movement evidently had been thought out and executed with consummate skill in the face of tremendous difficulties due to the weather.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt; he ladies and children were sent to aunpur and kbar in response to urgent entreaties from unim han that he would be pleased to come in person with all speed to the front, advanced to the famous ferry at haunsa where his father, mperor umayun, had suffered a severe defeat in 1539.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt; he army was then brought across to the southern bank of the river.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt;

 iege of atna 

atna had been under siege for several months now under unim han.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt; kbar continued his journey by water and on 3 ugust 1574 landed in the neighbourhood of atna. fter taking counsel with his officers and ascertaining that the besieged city relied for the greater part of its supplies on the town of ajipur situated on the opposite or northern bank of the anges he decided that the capture of that place was a necessary preliminary to the successful accomplishment of the main design. he difficulties caused by the flooded state of the huge river many miles in width at that season and the strenuous resistance of a strongly posted garrison were overcome and the fort was captured by the gallantry of the detachment appointed by kbar to the duty.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt; he heads of the fghan leaders killed were thrown into a boat and brought to kbar who forwarded them to aud as a hint of the fate which awaited and in due course befell him.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt;

he same day kbar ascended the anj ahari or ive ills a group of extremely ancient artificial mounds standing about half a mile to the south of the city and thence reconnoitred the position. aud, although he still had at his disposal 20,000 horses, a large park of artillery and many elephants, came to the conclusion that he could not resist the imperial power and decided on flight.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt; uring the night he slipped out quietly by a back gate and went to engal. he garrison which attempted to escape in the darkness suffered heavy losses in the process. kbar was eager to start at once but was persuaded to wait until the morning when he entered atna by the elhi gate.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt; e then personally pursued the fugitives for about 50 miles but failed to overtake them.

n enormous amount of booty including 265 elephants was taken and the common people enjoyed themselves picking up purses of gold and articles of armour in the streams and on the banks.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt; he capture of so great a city in the middle of the rainy season was an almost unprecedented achievement and a painful surprise to the engal ultan.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt; e had reckoned on kbar following the good old ndian custom of waiting until the asahara festival in ctober to begin a campaign. ut kbar disregarded adverse weather conditions and so was able to win victories in defiance of the shastras and the seasons.

 kbar returns to atehpur ikri 

he question now came up for decision whether the campaign should be prosecuted notwithstanding the rains or postponed until the cold season. pinions were divided but kbar had no hesitation in deciding that delay could not be permitted. ccordingly, he organised an additional army of more than 20,000 men entrusting the supreme command to old unim han who was appointed governor of engal.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt; aja odar al and other capable officers were placed under his orders aunpur, ttar radeshaunpur, enares, hunar and certain other territories were brought under the direct administration of the rown and officers were appointed to govern them on behalf of kbar.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt; e resolved to return to his capital leaving the engal campaign to be conducted by his generals. ate in eptember while he was encamped at hanpurdndatearch 2020 in the aunpur district he received dispatches announcing the success of unim han. he emperor arrived at atehpur ikri on 18 anuary 1575 after seven months of strenuous travelling and campaigning.

 attle 

he ughal army marched into the capital of engal, anda near auda cityaur, and aud withdrew to disha. he action was forced on unim han who was compelled to engage before he was ready. n the early stages of the conflict the ughal commander received several severe wounds and victory seemed assured to the engal army. ut later in the day the fall of auds general ujar han caused fortune to change sides and brought about the total defeat of aud who fled from the field.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt;

 reaty of atak and ftermath 

he battle led to the reaty of atak in which aud ceded the whole of engal and ihar, retaining only disha.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt; he treaty eventually failed after the death of unim han who died at the age of 80. ultan aud han took the opportunity and invaded engal. his would lead to the attle of aj ahal in 1576.lt;ref namequot;ndia 1889quot; /gt;

      text bytes1999 xmlspacepreserveileiuseppecampora.jpgrightthumbiuseppe ampora. iuseppe ampora eptember 30, 1923 – ecember 5, 2004 was an talytalian operatic tenor.

arly life
iuseppe ampora was born on eptember 30, 1923 in ortona, taly.

areer
ampora was a iacomo ucciniuccinian tenor. n 1954 he was the dubbed voice for icolai ilacuridi as inkerton in the armine allone directed film of adama utterfly.
  
ampora enjoyed successes in all the major theatres of taly including aurizio in driana ecouvreur with agda livero at the eatro alla cala, 1958, as well as at the etropolitan pera in ew ork ity, where his performances of the 1950s and 1960s are still fondly remembered.citation neededdateanuary 2012  e was the dgardo in ucia di ammermoor, in aria allass only et broadcast, in 1956.  n 1973, he debuted at the ew ork ity pera as the hevalier des rieux, in anon.  n 1980, he was heard at the an iego pera in ie ledermaus, opposite ame oan utherland and everly ills, in their only joint appearance. e also frequently sang the music of fellow ortonese orenzo erosi.

is discography includes recordings of a forza del destino 1952, a ioconda 1952, adama utterfly with enata ebaldi, 1952, imon occanegra with ictoria de los Ángeles, ito obbi and oris hristoff, 1957, osca with ebaldi and nzo ascherini, 1952 and a traviata 1952.

eath
ampora died on ecember 5, 2004.

empnett hrubwell is a small village and ivil parishes in nglandcivil parish in dairying country on the western edge of ath and orth ast omerset, in the county of omerset, ngland. t is about 15amp;nbsp;km south-west of ristol. he parish, which has a population of 177,lt;ref namequot;popnquot;/gt; is sheltered by the endip ills, near the iver eo ongresbury eoiver eo in the hew alley. t is the site of the airy oot oval tumulusbarrow.

ying just to the north of lagdon ake, isolated empnett hrubwell falls within the network of minor roads bounded by the 38 road38, 368 road368, 3114 and 3130; whilst signposted from each of these major routes, a lack of any further signposting makes it difficult to locate the village when arriving by road. he landscape is characterized by isolated farmsteads, the vernacular older buildings generally of the local arly urassicias limestone or of render with clay-tiled roofs.

hough being largely rurallt;refgt;cite webtitleural andscapes of ath and ortheast omerseturlhttp//www.bathnes.gov.uk/sites/default/files/rural_landscapes_-_chapters_1-6.pdfaccessdate16 ebruary 2018publisherath and omersetlt;/refgt; and consisting of one road and a few houses, empnett hrubwells curiously comedic name makes the village something of a famous local attraction.

t is the subject of the song own n empnett hrubwell by he urzels and is  mentioned in the earlier dge utler song p he lump.

 istory 
he name empnett hrubwell is believed to mean he grove at the village well from the eltic languageseltic langcelemetonnemett and the ld nglish langangwiell.lt;refgt;cite book lastobinson firsttephen authorlink coauthors titleomerset lace ames year1992 publisherhe ovecote ress td locationimborne, orset isbn1-874336-03-2lt;/refgt;

he parish of empnett hrubwell was part of the eynsham hundredeynsham undred county subdivisionundred,lt;refgt;cite webtitleomerset undredsurlhttp//www.genuki.org.uk/big/eng//iscellaneous/publisheraccessdate15 ctober 2011lt;/refgt;

 he airy oot 
mainairy oot

n the parish, the airy oot is an extensive oval barrow, formerly a chambered cairn which is a cheduled ncient onument, on the national monument register as 22826.lt;refgt;cite web  titlehe airy oot long barrow 350 m  of owgrove arm  worknglish eritages ecord of cheduled onuments  urlhttp//www.magic.gov.uk/rsm/22826.pdf  accessdate12 ay 2006lt;/refgt; he airy oot south-southwest of owgrove arm is a mound 60 m long, 25 m wide and now 2.5 m high, retained by a stone wall. ts summit is covered with ash trees and shrubs.lt;refgt;cite web  titleairy oot  urlhttp//www.themodernantiquarian.com/post/21791  accessdate12 ay 2006lt;/refgt; ormerly it was considerably higher. n being opened in 1789 and essentially destroyed, it was found to contain two rows of cells, running from south to north, formed by immense stones set edgeways, and covered by others of larger dimensions. t the time it was conjectured to be a work of the ruids, but its origins are far older and probably date from the eolithic period.lt;refgt;cite web  titleempnett hrubwell  work  urlhttp//www.genuki.org.uk/big/eng//empnetthrubwell/  accessdate12 ay 2006lt;/refgt;

ade and ade in their 1929 book quot;omersetquot; described it as quot;a remarkably fine tumulus of masonry, said to have been one of the finest in ritain, in the chambers of which skeletons have been discovered.  few vestiges of it now only remain, the rest has been used as a lime-kiln.quot;lt;ref namequot;autogenerated1quot;gt;gutenbergno12287nameomerset by ade, .. amp; ade, ..lt;/refgt;

 ivil ar 

he village played a minor role in the nglish ivil ar 1640–1660, just prior to the taking of ristol by homas airfax, 3rd ord airfax of ameronairfaxs forces. he village lies on the direct route between ristol and herborne, omersetherborne, where airfaxs forces had rested after he attle of angport in uly 1645. liver romwellromwells cavalry is known to have stabled in the hamlet on the nights of 8–9 eptember 1645 just before airfax’s final assault on ristol on 10 eptember in which they played a critical role.lt;refgt;cite booklastordenfirstlairtitlehe nglish ivil ars 1640-1660publishereidenfeld amp; icolsonyear2009isbn978-0-297-84888-2lt;/refgt;

 overnance 

he arish councils of nglandparish council has responsibility for local issues, including setting an annual precept local rate to cover the council’s operating costs and producing annual accounts for public scrutiny. he parish council evaluates local planning applications and works with the local police, district council officers, and eighbourhood atch neighbourhood watch groups on matters of crime, security, and traffic. he parish councils role also includes initiating projects for the maintenance and repair of parish facilities, such as the village hall or community centre, playing fields and playgrounds, as well as consulting with the district council on the maintenance, repair, and improvement of highways, drainage, footpaths, public transport, and street cleaning. onservation matters including trees and listed buildings and environmental issues are also of interest to the council.

empnett hrubwell is part of the hew alley outh ard which is represented by one councillor on the  unitary authority of ath and orth ast omerset which was created in 1996, as established by the ocal overnment ct 1992. t provides a single tier of local government in the nited ingdomlocal government with responsibility for almost all local government functions within its area including planning permissionlocal planning and uilding regulations in the nited ingdombuilding control, local roads, council housing, environmental health, arket placemarkets and fairs, refuse collection, recycling, cemeteries, crematoria, leisure services, parks, and tourism. t is also responsible for ocal ducation uthorityeducation, social services, librarylibraries, main roads, public transport, rading tandardstrading standards, waste disposal and strategic planning, although fire, police and ambulance services are provided jointly with other authorities through the von ire and escue ervice, von and omerset onstabulary and the reat estern mbulance ervice.

ath and orth ast omersets area covers part of the eremonial counties of nglandceremonial county of omerset but it is administered independently of the non-metropolitan county. ts administrative headquarters is in ath, omersetath. etween 1 pril 1974 and 1 pril 1996, it was the ansdyke districtansdyke istricts of nglanddistrict and the ath, omersetity of ath of the county of von.lt;refgt;cite weburlhttp//www.opsi.gov.uk/si/si1995/ksi_19950493_en_1.htm titlehe von tructural hange rder 1995 accessdate9 ecember 2007 work url-statusdead archiveurlhttps//web.archive.org/web/20080130105206/http//www.opsi.gov.uk/si/si1995/ksi_19950493_en_1.htm archivedate30 anuary 2008 lt;/refgt; efore 1974 that the parish was part of the lutton ural istrict.lt;ref namecluttonrdgt;cite webtitlelutton urlhttp//www.visionofbritain.org.uk/unit/10107775work vision of ritain hrough imepublisherniversity of ortsmouthaccessdate4 anuary 2014lt;/refgt;

 eography 

he nearby meadows at lasters reen eadows are designated as a ite of pecial cientific nterest because it is an area of unimproved and traditionally managed species-rich meadows which support a neutral grassland community of a type which is now rare throughout ritain. he site is situated on the slopes fringing the arly urassicias ablelands and is underlain by haetianhaetic clays and, lower down the slope eupereuper ed arl. he slowly permeable clay soils are slightly calcareous in nature and this is reflected in elements of the flora. he site is characterised by the nationally rare ommon napweed entaurea nigra and rested og’s-tail ynosurus cristatus and dominant grasses include weet ernal-grass nthoxanthum odoratum, rested og’s-tail and orkshire og olcus lanatus, while uaking rass riza media and ellow at-grass risetum flavescens are also frequent. here is a high component of herb species throughout the meadows including aw-wort erratuta tinctoria, yer’s reenweed enista tinctoria, ommon napweed, epper-saxifrage ilaum silaus, evil’s-bit cabious uccisa pratensis, tachys officinalisetony tachys officinalis and piny estharrow nonis spinosa. he calcareous nature of the soil is reflected by the presence of rimula verisowslip rimula veris, airy lax inum catharticum, laucous edge arex flacca, ady’s edstraw alium verum and occasional alad urnet anguisorba minor. he meadows are bounded by hedges supporting numerous species including rataegus monogynaawthorn rataegus monogyna, ych lm lmus glabra, nglish lm lmus procera, orylus avellanaazel orylus avellana and ield aple cer campestre. edgerow trees include uropean shsh raxinus excelsior, weet hestnut astanea sativa, lex aquifoliumolly lex aquifolium and ak uercus sp.lt;refgt;http//www.english-nature.org.uk/citation/citation_photo/1004121.pdf nglish ature citation sheet for lasters reen eadows  . etrieved 16 uly 2006.lt;/refgt;

 eligious sites 

he parish church, hurch of t ary, empnett hrubwellt arys on nap ill, has a tower containing five bells. he tower has set back buttresses and two arch bell openings with tracery. he tower is crowned by a parapet with blank arcading, and square pinnacles, it also has a slightly higher stair turret. he late ictorian chancel of 1897 is in the decorated style. nside the church is a screen attributed to ugin, although ikolaus evsner is of the opinion the architect is probably ugustus uginugin the younger.lt;ref namequot;pevsnerquot;gt;cite book  author  evsner, ikolaus  year  1958  title  he uildings of ngland  orth omerset and ristolpublisher  enguin ooksisbn0-14-071013-2 lt;/refgt; t is a rade * listed building,lt;refgt;  deschurch of t. ary  num1136164  accessdate9 ay 2006lt;/refgt; with a cross in the churchyard being listed rade .lt;refgt;  descegilbury ark arm  num1129641  accessdate9 ay 2006lt;/refgt;

he parish register lists christenings, marriages and burials from 1568. he lords of the manor and chief landowners, following the demise of the abers during the 17th century, have been the aron hartonbaronets ynte of alswell.lt;refgt;cite webtitleeeds, etc. of emeys-ynte and harton, alswell ouse, oathursturlhttp//www.nationalarchives.gov.uk/a2a/records.aspxcat168-ddrnamp;cid-1#-1publisherational rchivesaccessdate2 ctober 2010lt;/refgt; he yntes are probably responsible for the obelisk located at ookery arm in the parish.
